Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
12 min
The Tawqifi Nature of Quranic Order: A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Establishing that verse and surah order is tawqifi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the order of Quranic surahs and verses, identify the proofs (ijma and tawatur), explain the opposing view, and apply the ruling to the obligation of surah order in salah.

Core Idea
The order of Quranic verses and surahs is definitively from Allah, transmitted by tawatur — no human ijtihad is involved.

This passage tackles a foundational usul question: Is the arrangement of the Quran's chapters and verses a matter of divine direction (tawqif) or human inference? While verse order is uncontroversially tawqifi, the order of surahs has been debated. The author marshals ijma, tawatur, and prophetic practice to settle the matter, with practical implications for salah recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: whether the order of surahs in the Quran is tawqifi (divinely ordained) or based on ijtihad of the Companions.
Verse order is agreed upon; the dispute is only about surah order.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proofs
The Hanafi school holds that both verse and surah order are tawqifi. Identify the proofs: consensus (ijma) of Ahl al-Sunnah, tawatur of the mushaf, the Prophet’s annual presentation to Jibril, and explicit commands to place verses in specific surahs.
The passage emphatically rejects variant mushaf reports as weak.
3
Examine the opposing view and its evidence
Some scholars (Ibn Faris, Malik in one view) argued for ijtihad. Their evidence includes differences in early mushafs (Ali, Ibn Mas'ud) and Uthman's handling of al-Anfal and Bara'ah.
The passage dismisses these as illusory or misconstrued.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and practical consequence
The Hanafi response: tawatur overrides isolated reports; the al-Anfal/Bara'ah incident is about Basmala, not order; the dispute is verbal. The practical result is that surah order is wajib in salah, and missing it requires repetition (i'ada), though the prayer remains valid.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows the real impact of the usul position.

Source Text

(تتمة) أجمع أهل الحق - أعني أهل السنة والجماعة القاصمين للبدعة ـ على أن ترتيب آي كل سورة توقيفي بأمر الله وبأمر الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وعلى هذا انعقد الاجماع لا شبهة فيه وتواتر بلا شبهة عنه صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه، وفي «الاتقان» هذا الاجماع نقله غير واحد منهم الزركشي في «البرهان»، وأبو جعفر بن الزبير وقال : وعبارته هكذا: ترتيب الآيات في سورها واقع بتوقيفه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم من غير خلاف هذا في بين المسلمين وما روي عن أمير المؤمنين علي كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام أنه جمع آيات القرآن على ترتيب النزول لا على هذا الترتيب وقد روي عن الزهري قال : لو وجد لكان أنفع وأكثر علماً. فلم يصح عنه، والذي روى عنه قال: لما مات رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم آليت أن لا آخذ علي ردائي إلا لصلاة جمعة حتى أجمع القرآن فجمعته وقال الشيخ ابن حجر هذا الأثر ضعيف، ثم كيف يصح جمعه الآيات على ترتيب النزول وهو شاك في آية عدة الوفاة بالأشهر، وآية عدة ذوات الحمل أيهما مقدم نزولاً، وقد صح هذا عنه، ومثله صح في آيات أخرى وقد قال عكرمة عند سؤال محمد بن سيرين : ألفوه كما أنزل الأول فالأول، لو اجتمعت الإنس والجن على أن يؤلفوه ذلك التأليف ما استطاعوا ولو سلم هذه الرواية فالجمع جمع الصدر لا المصحف، وحفظ نزول الآيات لا الجمع للقراءة . بقي أمر ترتيب السور، فالمحققون على أنه من أمر الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وقيل هذا الترتيب باجتهاد من الصحابة واستدل عليه ابن فارس باختلاف المصاحف في ترتيب السور، فمصحف أمير المؤمنين علي كان على ترتيب النزول، ومصحف ابن مسعود على غير هذا، والذي الآن والحق هو الأول، وهذه الروايات مزخرفة موهومة، ولم توجد في الكتب المعتبرة ولا يعبأ بها في مقابلة التوارث الذي جرى من لدن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إلى الآن، وفي الاتقان ناقلاً عن الزركشي الخلاف لفظي، فمن قال إنه ليس توقيفياً فمراده لم يقع توقيفاً قولياً مصرحاً، بل علموا برمزه صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وآله وأصحابه والقرائن الأخرى الدالة، لكن هذه الدلالة قطعية من غير ريبة والذي يدل على هذه أن الإرادة قول مالك : إنما ألفوا القرآن على ما كانوا يستمعونه من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع قوله : بأن ترتيب السور عن اجتهاد، وقد نص البيهقي على أن القرآن كان على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم مرتباً سوره وآياته على هذا الترتيب، إلا أنه استثنى الأنفال وبراءة، واستدل بما روى أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وابن حبان والحاكم عن ابن عباس قال : قلت لعثمان : ما حملكم على أن عمدتم إلى الأنفال وهي من المثاني، وإلى براءة وهي من المئيين، فقرنتم بينهما ولم تكتبوا بينهما سطر بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، ووضعتموهما في السبع الطوال؟ فقال عثمان : كان رسول الله لا ينزل عليه السور ذوات العدد، وكان إذا نزل عليه الشيء دعا بعض من كان يكتب فيقول : ضعوا هؤلاء الآيات في السورة التي يذكر فيها كذا وكذا» وكانت الأنفال من أوائل ما نزل بالمدينة، وكانت براءة من آخر القرآن نزلاً وكانت قصتها شبيهة بقصتها، فظننت أنها منها، فقبض رسول الله له ولم يبين أنها منها، فمن أجل ذلك قرنت بينهما ولم أكتب بينهما سطر بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، ووضعتهما في السبع الطوال. كذا في «الاتقان». ولا يخفى على من له أدنى تدبر وخدمة بالعلوم الدينية أن استثناء البيهقي غير صحيح، كيف وجميع السور منقولة بالتواتر في المواضع التي كتبت فيها الآن فالقول بأن البعض كذا والبعض كذا تحكم ظاهر، والذين رووا عن أمير المؤمنين عثمان رضي الله تعالى عنه لا يدل على هذا أصلاً، ومعنى الخ، أنه قبض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ولم يبين قوله : فقبض براءة من الأنفال أم لا، لا أنه لم يبين موضعه الذي الآن فيه، وهذا كناية عن أنه لم أنه لم يأمر بكتابة الله الرحمن الرحيم، والمقصود تبيين هذا، والذي يدل على ما قلنا ما في «الدرر المنثورة» من رواية النحاس في ناسخه عن أمير المؤمنين عثمان عفان قال : كانت الأنفال وبراءة تدعيان في زمن رسول الله له بالقرينتين، فلذلك جعلتهما في السبع الطوال، فقد وضح وبان لك أن هذا الترتيب المتوارث المتواتر بلا شبهة فيما بين الآيات والسور من عند الله تعالى قطعاً، وعلمت أن براءة موضعها هذا الذي وضعت فيه من عند الله تعالى قطعاً. إلا أنه لم يؤمر بكتابة الله الرحمن الرحيم، فلها نوع التصاق بالأنفال، شبهاً بالأجزاء، لا أنها جزء منه حقيقة، وقال الكرماني : كان النبي الله يعرض القرآن على جبريل في كل سنة على هذا الترتيب، وفي السنة الآخرة عرض مرتين، وقد سمعت عن مطلع الأسرار الإلهية أبي قدس سره مراراً كثيرة أن الترتيب الذي بين السور في المصاحف هو من الله تعالى، وكان يشدد حتى يرى مراعاته واجباً في الصلاة ويقول : أمرنا بقراءة القرآن على هذا الترتيب، وكنت متعجباً من الحكم بالوجوب، حتى رأيت في البحر الرائق أن مراعاة الترتيب بين السور واجبة من واجبات القراءة في الصلاة، وكان أبي قدس سره يعيد الصلاة إذا فاته الترتيب بسهو ويأمر بالإعادة، كما وقع مرة من رجل تقديم سورة التين على ألم نشرح في العشاء، وكان هو مقتدياً، فأعاد وأمرهم بالإعادة، وكنت عرضت عليه أنه لم تفسد الصلاة؟ قال : نعم لم تفسد الصلاة، لكن الإعادة ألزم . ثم سمعت في مجلس آخر بناءه على هذا. واعلم أيضاً أنه كما يجب تواتر كل جزء من أجزاء القرآن كذلك يجب تواتر عدد السور.
(Appendix) The people of truth—that is, Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah who break innovation—have agreed that the arrangement of the verses of every surah is tawqifi (divinely ordained) by the command of Allah and by the command of the Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace. And upon this the consensus was concluded, no doubt in it, and it is transmitted (tawatur) without doubt from him, may the blessings of Allah be upon him and his family and companions. In al-Itqan, this consensus is narrated by more than one, among them al-Zarkashi in al-Burhan, and Abu Ja'far ibn al-Zubayr, and he said: His expression is thus: The arrangement of verses in their surahs occurred by his tawqif, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, without any difference among Muslims. And what is narrated from the Commander of the Faithful Ali, may Allah ennoble his face and the faces of his noble family, that he collected the verses of the Quran according to the order of revelation, not according to this arrangement—and it is narrated from al-Zuhri that he said: If it were found, it would be more beneficial and more knowledgeable. But it is not authentically proven from him. And what is narrated from him said: When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, died, I vowed that I would not put on my cloak except for Friday prayer until I collected the Quran, so I collected it. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said this report is weak. Then how can his collection of verses according to the order of revelation be authentic, while he was in doubt about the verse of the waiting period (iddah) of widows in months and the verse of the waiting period of pregnant women—which of them preceded in revelation? This is authentically proven from him. Similarly, it is proven for other verses. And Ikrimah said, when asked by Muhammad ibn Sirin: Compose it as it was revealed, first then first. If humans and jinn gathered to compile it in that compilation, they could not. Even if this narration is accepted, the collection is a collection of the chest (memorization), not the mushaf (written codex), and preservation of the revelation order of verses, not collection for recitation. The matter of the order of surahs remains: the verifiers (muhaqqiqun) say it is from the command of the Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace. And it is said this order is by ijtihad of the Companions. Ibn Faris adduced as evidence the difference of mushafs in the order of surahs: the mushaf of the Commander of the Faithful Ali was according to the order of revelation, and the mushaf of Ibn Mas'ud was different. But what is [the order] now—and the truth is the first view. These narrations are embellished and illusory, not found in reliable books, and are not to be considered in the face of the successive transmission that has passed from the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, until now. In al-Itqan, quoting al-Zarkashi, the disagreement is verbal: whoever says it is not tawqifi means it did not occur as an explicit verbal tawqif, but they learned it through his (the Prophet's) hint, may blessings and peace be upon him and his family and companions, and other indicators. But this indication is definitive without doubt. And what indicates this is the will of Malik: They only compiled the Quran based on what they used to hear from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, along with his statement that the order of surahs is by ijtihad. Al-Bayhaqi stated that the Quran in the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, was arranged in its surahs and verses according to this order, except that he excepted al-Anfal and Bara'ah. He adduced the hadith narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim from Ibn Abbas who said: I said to Uthman: What made you take al-Anfal, which is from the Mathani, and Bara'ah, which is from the Mi'in, and join them together without writing the line 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' between them, and you placed them among the seven long (surahs)? Uthman replied: The Messenger of Allah used to receive surahs with multiple [verses]. When something was revealed, he would call some of the scribes and say: Place these verses in the surah where such-and-such is mentioned. Al-Anfal was among the earliest revealed in Medina, and Bara'ah was among the last revealed in the Quran, and their story was similar. So I thought it belonged to it. Then the Messenger of Allah was taken (died) and he did not clarify whether it was from it. For that reason I joined them together and did not write the line 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' between them, and I placed them in the seven long (surahs). Thus in al-Itqan. It is not hidden from anyone with the least reflection and service in religious sciences that al-Bayhaqi's exception is incorrect. How so, when all surahs are transmitted via tawatur in the positions where they are written now. So saying that some are such and some are such is an apparent arbitrary judgment. Those who narrated from the Commander of the Faithful Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, do not indicate this at all. And the meaning of 'he did not clarify' is that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, was taken (died) and did not clarify his statement: whether Bara'ah is from al-Anfal or not, not that he did not clarify its place where it is now. This is a metaphor for the fact that he (the Prophet) did not command to write 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. And the purpose is to clarify this. What indicates what we said is found in al-Durr al-Manthur from the narration of al-Nahhas in his Nasikh from the Commander of the Faithful Uthman ibn Affan who said: Al-Anfal and Bara'ah used to be called in the time of the Messenger of Allah 'the two companions' (al-qarinatayn), so for that reason I placed them among the seven long (surahs). Thus it is clear and evident to you that this inherited, successively transmitted order without doubt among verses and surahs is from Allah, the Exalted, definitively. And you have known that Bara'ah's place is this very place where it is placed, from Allah, the Exalted, definitively. But it was not commanded to write 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', so it has a kind of attachment to al-Anfal, resembling parts, not that it is truly a part of it. Al-Kirmani said: The Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would present the Quran to Gabriel every year in this order, and in the final year he presented it twice. I have heard from the key to divine secrets, my father (quddisa sirruhu), many times that the order between surahs in the mushafs is from Allah, the Exalted, and he would insist, even regarding it obligatory to observe in prayer, saying: We have been commanded to recite the Quran in this order. I was amazed at the ruling of obligation until I saw in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that observing order between surahs is obligatory from the obligations of recitation in prayer. My father, may his secret be sanctified, would repeat the prayer if he missed the order due to forgetfulness and would order repetition. As happened once with a man who presented Surah al-Tin before Alam Nashrah (al-Inshirah) in the Isha prayer, and he was following (as imam). So he repeated and ordered them to repeat. I presented to him that the prayer was not invalidated? He said: Yes, the prayer is not invalidated, but repetition is necessary. Then I heard in another session based on this. Know also that just as tawatur is incumbent for every part of the Quran, so too is tawatur incumbent for the number of surahs.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This lengthy appendix (tammah) addresses a fundamental usul issue: the ordering of Quranic verses and surahs. The author affirms the consensus (ijma) of Ahl al-Sunnah that the arrangement of verses within each surah is tawqifi (divinely ordained by explicit prophetic instruction). For surah order, the majority of verifiers (muhaqqiqun) hold it is tawqifi as well, though some attributed it to ijtihad of the Companions. The author rejects reports of variant surah orders (like Mus'haf Ali and Ibn Mas'ud) as baseless or misunderstood. The hadith of Uthman about al-Anfal and Bara'ah shows that their placement without Basmala was due to ambiguity, not ijtihad. Ultimately, the author concludes both verse and surah order are definitively from Allah, transmitted by tawatur. As a practical ramification, he cites a ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that maintaining surah order in salah is obligatory (wajib), and missing it deliberately or forgetfully necessitates repetition (i'ada), though the prayer is valid. The passage ends by emphasizing that tawatur is required for the number of surahs just as for their content.

Key Terms
توقيفي (tawqifi): Divinely ordained by explicit command of Allah or the Prophet, not by human reasoning
تواتر (tawatur): Continuous transmission from many independent chains such that certainty is attained

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on observing the order of surahs in salah?
A) It is not required
B) It is a recommended sunnah
C) It is obligatory (wajib)
D) It invalidates the prayer if missed

Key Takeaway
The order of Quranic verses and surahs is definitively from Allah, transmitted by tawatur, and maintaining it in prayer is wajib.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
Silence of the Companions as Consensus (Ijma Suktuti) in the Case of al-Maghrur
Proving that silence of Sahabah constitutes ijma on non-valuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the silence of the Sahabah in the case of al-maghrur constitutes ijma suktuti and apply the Hanafi principle that silence in a context of need indicates consensus.

Core Idea
When the Companions remain silent on a legal issue needing clarification, their silence itself is evidence of the ruling.

The Hanafi school recognizes silent consensus (ijma suktuti) as a valid source of law. This lesson examines a classic example: the Companions' unanimous view that the child of a deceived buyer (al-maghrur) is free upon payment of its price, but their silence on whether the master is also owed compensation for the child's benefits. That silence, argues the author, proves the benefits are not compensable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the specific question about the benefits of al-maghrur's child? The Companions agreed the child is free by paying the price, but they did not discuss whether the true owner is compensated for the child's usufruct.
The benefits (manafi') refer to services or income derived from the child during the period before the truth was known.
2
Recognize the Companions' position
They explicitly held consensus on the child being free with a price, but remained silent on the valuation of benefits. This silence is not passive; it occurs in a context where clarification is expected.
The silence is significant because the issue directly affects financial rights.
3
Apply the principle of dalaalat al-haal
The state (haal) of the silent person indicates the ruling. Here, the Companions' noble character and their duty to clarify when needed mean their silence indicates that benefits are not compensable.
If benefits were compensable, the Companions would have spoken to prevent injustice.
4
Distinguish from neutral silence
Not all silence is evidence. The Hanafi principle requires that the silence occur in a situation where the scholar is expected to speak (e.g., a new legal problem). The al-maghrur case meets that condition.
Compare: silence on a matter not requiring clarification carries no weight.
5
Evaluate the evidentiary strength
Ijma suktuti is zanni al-thubut (transmission is not absolutely certain) but qati al-dalala (meaning is clear once established). The passage argues that here it is strong enough to derive a ruling.
The rule 'affirm it, do not advance or delay' means accept this proof without alteration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها دلالة حال الساكت على حكم المسكوت كسكوت الصحابة عن تقويم منافع ولد المغرور وهو الذي تزوج امرأة يظنها حرة أو اشترى أمة يزعمها ملكاً للبائع فولدت له ولداً ثم ظهر أنها أمة المستحق، وولد المغرور حرّ بالقيمة، على ذلك انعقد إجماع الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وسكتوا عن تبيين تقويم منافعه وتضمين قيمتها (يفيد) هذا السكوت عدم تقومها شرعاً للمولى) فلا يلزمه قيمة المنافع عليه (وإلا) أي وإن كان تقومها للمولى (الزم) الكتمان عند وجوب البيان فإنه وقت الحاجة إليه، والكتمان عندها معصية والصحابة محفوظون عنها فسكوتهم بمنزلة إجماعهم بدلالة حالهم الشريفة، فاثبت ولا تقدم ولا تؤخر
And among them is the indication of the state of the silent one regarding the ruling of the unspoken, like the silence of the Companions regarding the valuation of the benefits of the child of al-maghrur. He is the one who married a woman thinking she was free, or bought a slave-girl claiming she was the property of the seller, and she bore him a child, then it appeared that she was the slave of the rightful owner. The child of al-maghrur is free by paying the price. Upon that, the consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, was held, and they remained silent about explaining the valuation of its benefits and including its value. This silence indicates its non-valuation legally for the master, so he is not liable for the value of the benefits. And otherwise, i.e., if it were valuable for the master, concealment would be necessary when clarification is obligatory, for it is a time of need for it, and concealment at that time is a sin, and the Companions are protected from it. So their silence is like their consensus by the indication of their noble state. So affirm it, and do not advance or delay.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents a third example of the indication of silence: the silence of the Sahabah (Companions) regarding whether the benefits (usufruct) of a child born to a deceived purchaser (al-maghrur) should be valued and paid to the true owner. The Sahabah agreed that the child is free by paying the price, but they remained silent on whether the master of the child (the true owner) is owed compensation for the benefits derived from the child during the period before the truth was known. The author argues that this silence indicates that such benefits are not legally compensable (not muqawwam). If they were compensable, the Sahabah would have been obliged to clarify, as it was a matter of need. Their silence, being protected from sin, thus constitutes implicit consensus (ijma suktuti). The passage emphasizes that the silence of the Sahabah in this context carries the weight of consensus.

Key Terms
إجماع سكوتي (ijma suktuti): Consensus established by the silence of qualified scholars when an issue arises and they do not object.
المغرور (al-maghrur): A person who is deceived; here, one who marries or buys a slave under the false impression that she is free or owned by the seller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the Companions' silence on the valuation of the benefits of the child of al-maghrur proves that:
A) The benefits are compensable to the master.
B) The benefits are not compensable to the master.
C) The child is not free.
D) The silence is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the silence of the Companions on a legal issue that required clarification is a binding proof (ijma suktuti) of the implied ruling.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
10 min
Consensus Cannot Be Abrogated or Abrogate
Explaining the rule that ijma is not subject to naskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that ijma is not subject to naskh and evaluate the rational arguments supporting its immutability.

Core Idea
Ijma is a definitive proof (qat'i) — it cannot be abrogated by speculative evidence, nor can it be the agent of abrogation.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut explores a foundational principle of Hanafi usul: the immunity of consensus (ijma) from abrogation. The author presents a logical argument that consensus, once formed on a non-time-bound ruling, indicates the ruling is inherently good or evil and thus permanent. The discussion also addresses the possibility of abrogation by later evidence and refines the scope to decisive (qat'i) ijma. Master this rule to understand why certain rulings in the Hanafi school are considered final and unchangeable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Scope
State the two-part claim: ijma cannot be abrogated (mansukh) and cannot abrogate (nasikh). Note that the passage says this is the view of the majority (al-jumhur).
The phrase 'عند الجمهور' indicates this is the dominant position, with some opposing.
2
Understand the Rationale for Non-Abrogability
Examine why ijma cannot be abrogated: the agreement of all mujtahids on a non-time-bound ruling indicates the ruling is intrinsically good or evil (hasan/qabih li-dhatihi). Such rulings are not susceptible to being lifted, so naskh is impossible.
If the ruling were time-bound, it lapses naturally; that is not considered naskh.
3
Analyze the Logical Proof Against Abrogation
Work through the author's disjunctive argument: abrogation would have to be by speculative (zanni) or decisive (qat'i) evidence. Zanni cannot override qat'i ijma. Decisive evidence must come from a transmitted report (naql) or another ijma. Both are impossible for the reasons given (timing, authority, and the Prophet's presence).
The argument is a classic dalil aqli (rational proof) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the Refinement on Type of Ijma
The author suggests that the discussion should be restricted to qat'i ijma (consensus based on definitive evidence). Silent consensus (sukuti) or ijma transmitted by ahad reports may not share the same immunity.
This refinement avoids overgeneralization.
5
Consider the Prior Abrogator Objection
Reflect on the nuance: a prior decisive text that is an abrogator does not make the subsequent ijma erroneous, because naskh lifts the ruling after its establishment, not from the beginning. The author of the base text allowed the abrogator to be prior, which invites further reflection.
This shows the depth of the debate within Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: (الإجماع لا يكون منسوخاً ولا ناسخاً عند الجمهور) خلافاً للبعض (أما الأول : فلما أقول اتفاق الكل على حكم من غير تأقيت يدل على أنه حسن أو قبيح) لذاته (لا يحتمل السقوط فلا ينسخ، لما أن الحسن الذي لا يحتمل السقوط وكذا القبيح كذلك لا يقبل النسخ (وإلا) يكن حسناً أو قبيحاً كذلك الجاز الاختلاف عادة) فلا يصح انعقاد الإجماع. فالحكم المجمع عليه الغير الموقت لا ينسخ ، وأما الموقت فظاهر أنه ينتفي بانتفاء الوقت، وهو ليس من النسخ في شيء قال (مطلع الأسرار (الإلهية والدي قدس سره العزيز: لا حد أن الملازمة، لأنه من الجائز أن يكون أهل الإجماع الثلاثة أو الاثنين، فيجوز أن لا يختلف فيه، والعادة غير محيلة، وأيضاً يجوز أن يكون المستند خبراً من أخبار الآحاد مقطوع الدلالة، فلا يختلف أصلاً، وإن كان أهل الإجماع جماً غفيراً، ثم هذا إنما يتم إذا وجب الإجماع المستند، وأما إذا جوز الإجماع من إلهام الله تعالى الغير المكذوب فلا يحتمل الاختلاف أصلاً، هذا واستدل بأن انتساخ الإجماع بظني أو قطعي والأول باطل، لأن (نسخه بالظني خلاف المعقول لأن الإجماع قطعي والثاني إما نقل أو إجماع لا ثالث، والأول باطل لأنه إما متأخر عن الإجماع (وبنقل قاطع متأخر لا يتصور) الانتساخ (إذ لا إجماع إلا بعده عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام) إذ لا اعتداد لفتوى أحد بحضرته الشريفة، لا اعتداد بالإجماع من غير دخوله صلاة الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه والسلام، أو متقدم على الإجماع (وبـ) نقل (متقدم) قاطع ( يجعله خطأ) لأن الفتوى على خلاف النص القاطع الغير المنسوخ باطل، وأيضاً : الناسخ يجب تأخيره والثاني أيضاً ،باطل لأنه لا بد حينئذ من إجماع قاطع لدوام الأول وبإجماع آخر يمتنع، إذ لا ولاية للأمة على قطع الدوام للحكم (وإدراك الانتهاء) ثم الأولى أن يحذف الشق الأول من البين فإنه يختص حينئذ البيان بالإجماع المقطوع دون السكوتي والمنقول آحاداً، بل يقال : إن انتساخه بنقل أو إجماع إلى الآخر، ثم ربما يناقش بأن النقل القاطع المتقدم إذا كان ناسخاً لا يجعل الإجماع خطأ، فإن الناسخ يرتفع به المنسوخ بعد ثبوته، لا أنه يبطل به من بدء الأمر، والمصنف جوز كون الناسخ مقدماً فتأمل فيه، فإنه موضع (
Issue: (Consensus is neither abrogated nor abrogating according to the majority) contrary to some. (As for the first): Because I say: The agreement of all on a ruling without a time-limit indicates that it is good or evil in essence, not susceptible to falling away, so it cannot be abrogated. For that which is good and not susceptible to falling away, and similarly evil, does not accept abrogation. Otherwise, if it were not good or evil in that way, disagreement would be possible ordinarily, so consensus would not be validly concluded. Thus a consensus ruling not time-bound cannot be abrogated. As for a time-bound ruling, it obviously ceases with the end of time, and that is not naskh at all. The author of Matali' al-Asrar (my revered father) said: There is no necessity in the implication, because it is possible that the people of consensus are only three or two, so it is possible that disagreement does not occur, and custom does not prevent it. Also it is possible that the basis is a report from ahad reports that is definitive in indication (qat'i al-dalala), so disagreement does not occur at all, even if the consensus group is large. Then this holds only if the consensus must be based on a source (mustanad). As for if consensus is allowed to be from divine inspiration (ilham) that is not erroneous, then disagreement is impossible at all. This is the proof that abrogation of consensus by speculative or decisive [evidence] is invalid. The first is invalid because abrogating it by speculative evidence is contrary to reason since consensus is decisive. The second either comes via a transmitted report or another consensus, no third. The first (transmitted report) is invalid because it is either after the consensus (and a decisive report after consensus cannot conceive of naskh, because there is no consensus except after it, upon him and his family and companions, peace and blessings, since no fatwa of anyone in his noble presence is considered, nor is consensus considered without his entry, peace and blessings upon him and his family and companions), or it is before the consensus (and a decisive prior report would make the consensus erroneous, because giving a fatwa contrary to a decisive non-abrogated text is invalid). Also, the abrogator must be later. The second (consensus) is also invalid because then it would require a decisive consensus for the continuity of the first, and another consensus to abrogate, which is impossible, as the community has no authority to cut off the continuity of a ruling or to perceive its end. Then it is better to delete the first part of the disjunction, because then the discussion is specific to decisive consensus, not silent consensus (sukuti) or transmitted by ahad. Rather it should be said: Its abrogation by a transmitted report or consensus [is invalid]. Then it may be discussed that a decisive transmitted report that is prior, if it is an abrogator, does not make the consensus erroneous, for the abrogator raises the abrogated after its establishment, not that it invalidates it from the beginning. The author allowed the abrogator to be prior, so reflect on this, for it is a place...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (mas'ala) on the nature of consensus (ijma) regarding abrogation (naskh). The author states the majority position: ijma cannot be abrogated, nor can it abrogate. He first explains why ijma cannot be abrogated: if the ruling is not time-bound, the consensus indicates that the ruling is good or evil in itself, and such rulings are permanent and cannot be abrogated. If the ruling were not inherently good or evil, disagreement would be possible, and consensus could not form. Thus, only time-bound consensus can lapse, but that is not considered naskh. The author then quotes 'Matali' al-Asrar' (probably a supercommentary) which criticizes the logical implication (mulazama) by noting that consensus could be formed by a small group (two or three) where disagreement might not occur habitually, and also that the basis could be an ahad report with definitive meaning (qat'i al-dalala), so the consensus would be definitive despite the report's speculative transmission. The argument then proceeds: abrogation of ijma could be by speculative (zanni) or decisive (qat'i) evidence. The speculative is invalid because ijma is decisive. The decisive either comes from a transmitted report or another ijma. A transmitted report cannot abrogate because if it comes after the ijma, it cannot be an abrogator because ijma was established after the report's time (especially during the Prophet's era, his presence prevents consensus without him). If the report is before the ijma, then the ijma would be erroneous because it contradicts a decisive text that is not abrogated. Also, the abrogator must be later, so a prior report cannot abrogate. Another ijma cannot abrogate because it would require a decisive consensus to continue the first, and another to abrogate, which is impossible as the community cannot arbitrarily end a ruling. The passage ends with a refinement: the discussion applies only to decisive (qat'i) ijma, not silent (sukuti) or ahad-transmitted ijma. It also notes a possible objection: a prior decisive report that is abrogative does not make the ijma erroneous because the abrogator raises the abrogated after its establishment, not from the beginning. The author (of the text being commented on) allowed the abrogator to be prior, so the reader should reflect.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the ummah on a ruling; a definitive proof (qat'i) in Hanafi usul.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation: the lifting of a ruling by a later evidence. In this context, the discussion is whether ijma can be the object or agent of naskh.
قطعي (qat'i): Definitive: a ruling or evidence that is certain and cannot be overturned by speculative (zanni) evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of a time-bound ruling established by consensus?
A) It can be abrogated by later evidence.
B) It lapses with the end of time, which is not considered naskh.
C) It becomes permanent and cannot be changed.
D) It must be based on a mutawatir report.

Key Takeaway
Consensus (ijma) in the Hanafi school is a decisive proof that is immune from abrogation and cannot itself abrogate, ensuring legal stability.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

Abrogation of Ijma and by Ijma
Explaining whether ijma can be abrogated and whether it can abrogate other sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the abrogation of ijma and evaluate the conditions under which a later consensus can override an earlier one.

Core Idea
Ijma is definitive, but non-Companion ijma may be abrogated by another ijma when maslaha changes.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut delves into the nuanced Hanafi position on the abrogation of ijma (consensus). While the majority holds that ijma is neither abrogated nor abrogative, later scholars like Fakhr al-Islam allowed abrogation of non-Companion ijma due to changing circumstances (maslaha). This lesson unpacks the proofs and counterarguments, distinguishing between Companion consensus (stronger) and later consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
The author asks: Is ijma subject to abrogation? The majority (Hanafi) says no, while some scholars allow it. Understand the two positions.
The dispute is about the possibility of later evidence overriding an earlier consensus.
2
State the majority Hanafi proof
The majority argues that ijma is definitive (qat'i); abrogation by conjectural evidence (zanni) is irrational. Definitive evidence must be either a transmitted proof or another ijma. A transmitted proof cannot work: if later, no ijma exists after the Prophet; if earlier, it makes the ijma erroneous. Another ijma is impossible because the ummah cannot terminate a ruling's continuity.
This is the standard argument summarized in the text.
3
Analyze the exception for non-Companion ijma
Later Hanafis, notably Fakhr al-Islam, allow abrogation of non-Companion ijma by another ijma when the benefit (maslaha) changes. Companion consensus is stronger and cannot be abrogated.
The text cites Fakhr al-Islam's apparent contradiction and resolves it.
4
Evaluate the inspiration-based ijma argument
Some proposed that ijma could be based on direct inspiration (ilham). The text rejects this because it would allow abrogation of the Quran and Sunnah, undermining the seal of prophethood.
The argument is refuted by the completion of religion (Ma'ida 5:3).
5
Apply the distinction
Practice identifying whether a given consensus is Companion or non-Companion. Only non-Companion ijma can be abrogated by another ijma due to changed maslaha.
This distinction determines the stability of early rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آتياً بها (لقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا يَكُونُ لِي أَنْ أُبَدِّلَمُ مِن تِلْقَابِي نَفْسِي إِنْ أَتَّبِعُ إِلَّا مَا يُوحَى إِلَى [يونس: ١٥] واعلم أنه روى الدارقطني أنه قال : رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: لا ينسخ كلامي كلام الله وكلام الله ينسخ كلامي وكلام الله ينسخ بعضه بعضاً» فهذا بظاهره يدل على أن السنة لا تنسخ الكتاب وأجاب الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي رحمه تعالى بأن المراد كلامي الذي استخرج بالرأي والاجتهاد فلا ينسخ كلام الله الذي هو الوحي، ويؤيد هذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْى يُوحَى ) [ النجم : ٣ - ٤] (فكل ما صدر عن اللسان الشريف من الكتاب والسنة وحي وكاشف عما في الكلام الأزلي)، فالانتساخ بالسنة في الحقيقة انتساخ حكم ثابت بكلامه وقال : يحتمل أن يكون هذا الحديث منسوخاً، وهو بظاهره خبر، فلا يحتمل النسخ، إلا أن يقال إنه إنشاء لوجوب العمل بالكتاب عند معارضة الحديث إياه في صورة الخبر لعدم الانتساخ به فافهم وتدبر .

على المنسوخ، فهو خطأ في نفس الأمر، وإن لم يعلم لعدم ظهور منسوخيته وعلى الثاني فالإجماع بإلهام من تعالى، وحينئذ يصح أن يكون منسوخاً وناسخاً، لكن كما أنه يصلح ناسخاً للإجماع، كذلك يصلح ناسخاً للكتاب والسنة، فإن الإلهام لا يكون باطلاً، فلا بد من أن يكون رافعاً، لكن على هذا يلغو الإجماع، ويكون إلهام الواحد أيضاً ناسخاً، ولا يجترىء على هذا أحد، فإن الفتوى من غير حجة شرعية بعد ظهور ختم النبوة صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم مما لا يجوز أصلاً هذا كلام متين غاية المتانة وليس لقائل أن يقول : فرق بين إلهام الواحد وإلهام الكل مخالفاً لما ثبت بالشريعة المطهرة فإن إلهام الواحد الرافع لما ثبت بها يوجب Coming with it (to His statement: {Say: It is not for me to change it of my own accord; I only follow what is revealed to me} [Yunus: 15]. Know that al-Daraqutni narrated that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'My speech does not abrogate the speech of Allah, and the speech of Allah abrogates my speech, and the speech of Allah abrogates some of it by other parts.' This, in its apparent meaning, indicates that the Sunnah does not abrogate the Book. Shaykh Abd al-Haqq al-Dihlawi (may Allah have mercy on him) replied that what is meant by 'my speech' is that which is derived by opinion and ijtihad, so it does not abrogate the speech of Allah which is revelation. This is supported by His statement: {Nor does he speak from desire; it is but revelation revealed} [Najm: 3-4]. So everything that issues from the noble tongue, whether Book or Sunnah, is revelation and discloses what is in the pre-eternal speech. Therefore, abrogation by the Sunnah is in reality abrogation of a ruling established by His speech. He said: It is possible that this hadith is abrogated, and in its apparent form it is a report, so it does not admit abrogation, unless it is said that it is a directive for the obligation of acting by the Book when a hadith contradicts it in the form of a report due to lack of abrogation by it. So understand and reflect.

Issue: (Consensus is not abrogated nor abrogative according to the majority) contrary to some. (As for the first: because I say agreement of all on a ruling without a time limit indicates that it is good or evil) in essence (does not admit of removal, so it is not abrogated, because the good that does not admit of removal, and similarly the evil, does not accept abrogation (otherwise) if it were not good or evil in that way, difference of opinion would be customary) so the formation of consensus would not be valid. So a ruling agreed upon without time limit is not abrogated. As for a time-bound ruling, it is apparent that it ceases with the cessation of time, and that is not abrogation at all. He said (Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya): May his noble secret be sanctified: There is no limit to the entailment, because it is possible that the people of consensus are three or two, so it is possible that no disagreement occurs in it, and custom does not prevent it. Also, it is possible that the basis is a report from solitary reports with definitive indication, so no disagreement occurs at all, even if the people of consensus are a great multitude. Then this is only complete if the consensus is based on a basis; but if consensus is allowed through inspiration from Allah that is not falsified, then it does not admit disagreement at all. This is argued by saying that abrogation of consensus is either by conjectural or definitive [evidence]. The first is invalid because (abrogation by conjectural is contrary to reason because consensus is definitive. The second is either a transmitted proof or consensus with no third. The first is invalid because it is either later than consensus (and by a definitive transmitted proof later, abrogation is not conceivable) (since there is no consensus except after it, blessings and peace be upon him and his family and companions) because the opinion of anyone in his noble presence is not considered, and consensus cannot be established without his inclusion, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, or earlier than consensus (and by an earlier definitive transmitted proof it makes it erroneous) because issuing a fatwa contrary to a definitive non-abrogated text is invalid. Also, the abrogator must be later. The second is also invalid because then there must be a definitive consensus for the continuation of the first, and by another consensus it is impossible, since the ummah has no authority to terminate the continuation of the ruling (and to perceive its ending). Then it is better to delete the first part from the discussion because then the explanation is specific to definitive consensus, not to silent consensus and that transmitted individually. Rather, it is said: Its abrogation is by a transmitted proof or consensus to the other. Then perhaps it can be debated that the earlier definitive transmitted proof, if it is an abrogator, does not make the consensus erroneous, because the abrogator raises the abrogated after its establishment, not that it invalidates it from the beginning. And the author allowed the abrogator to be earlier. So reflect on this, for it is a place for reflection.

(And in it is a clear consideration) For we do not concede that there is no authority to terminate the continuation, because the time for abrogation of what is established by revelation ended with his death, peace and blessings be upon him and his family, wives, and companions, but the time for abrogation of what is established by consensus did not end because of the possibility of its formation after him. So the expiration of the duration of its ruling is not prevented for the deeply learned mujtahids who are attentive to the secrets of the Sharia (due to change of benefit [maslaha]). So it is permissible for them to reach consensus contrary to what they previously agreed upon due to the possibility of a new benefit arising, unless) the first consensus (is the consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them (for it is stronger) than other consensuses (it is not abrogated by a consensus of those after them because invalidating the stronger by the weaker is not permissible. So in the apparent meaning of these two statements of the noble imam there is contradiction, but it is repelled by saying that his intent is to prevent abrogation of the Book and Sunnah by consensus, as his proof indicates, so it does not contradict abrogation of consensus by consensus. Then Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya said: May his secret be sanctified: Consensus is either based on a source or not. The requirement of a source is not obligatory by evidence. On the first, the ruling established by the first consensus is established beforehand, and so is the ruling of the second consensus. So abrogation, if it occurs, is by the two sources. Consensus is merely the proof of the abrogator, like the action of a Companion contrary to an explicit text. Then, if the source is qiyas, consensus is proof of the proof. Also, the first consensus then is consensus on the abrogated, so it is erroneous in itself, even if unknown due to lack of appearance of its abrogation. On the second, consensus is by inspiration from Allah, and then it can be abrogated and abrogative, but just as it can be abrogative of consensus, so too it can be abrogative of the Book and Sunnah, because inspiration is not false, so it must be elevating. But on this, consensus becomes meaningless, and the inspiration of a single person would also be abrogative, and no one would dare to say this, because issuing a fatwa without a legal proof after the appearance of the seal of prophecy (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) is not permissible at all. This is a very firm speech, and no one can say: There is a difference between the inspiration of one and the inspiration of all, contrary to what is established by the pure Sharia, because the inspiration of one that elevates what is established by it would necessitate no difference between him and the prophets of the Children of Israel, thus losing the benefit of the seal, unlike the inspiration of the people of consensus, because that does not necessitate impossibility. This is because the rulings have been perfected and the Sharia has been completed with the appearance of the Muhammadan seal (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions), as is indicated by His statement: {Today I have perfected for you your religion and completed My favor upon you and have chosen for you Islam as a religion} [Ma'ida: 3]. So no ruling appears after the death of the Seal (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him and his family and companions) that was not established, so correct inspiration is not valid, neither for one nor for all, regarding what is not established by the brilliant Sharia. So consensus, if allowed without a source but merely by inspiration, this inspiration is only in agreement with some proof, and denying this may be obstinate and far from what anyone would dare. So understand. And those who allow consensus to be abrogated (said: If the ummah differed on two opinions, then they reach consensus (that the matter is ijtihad, it is permissible to adopt either of the two opinions, so if they reach consensus on one of them, the permissibility of adopting the other becomes invalid).
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the abrogation (naskh) of consensus (ijma). It begins with a hadith from al-Daraqutni stating that the Prophet's speech does not abrogate Allah's speech, but Allah's speech abrogates His own speech and the Prophet's speech. This is interpreted to mean that the Sunnah derived from ijtihad does not abrogate the Quran. Then the main issue: whether ijma can be abrogated or abrogate. The majority holds that ijma is neither abrogated nor abrogative. For it being non-abrogable: a ruling unanimously agreed upon without time limit is either intrinsically good or evil, and such does not admit removal; if it were time-bound, its end is not abrogation. Matali' al-Asrar critiques this reasoning: the entailment that only a few people could form consensus is possible, and the basis could be a solitary hadith with definitive indication, preventing disagreement. But if consensus is based on divine inspiration, disagreement is impossible. Then an argument is presented: abrogation of ijma by conjectural evidence is unreasonable (since ijma is definitive), and by definitive evidence is either a transmitted proof or another ijma. If the transmitted proof comes later, abrogation is impossible because no ijma exists after the proof? Actually, the text says there is no consensus after the Prophet's time? It seems confused: it says no consensus except after him, so later proof can't abrogate? Then if the proof is earlier, it would make the ijma erroneous (since the ruling would contradict a definitive text). Also, the abrogator must be later, so an earlier proof cannot abrogate. The other possibility (abrogation by another ijma) is also invalid because the ummah has no authority to terminate a ruling's continuity. However, the author notes that some allow it due to change of benefit (maslaha) except for the consensus of the Companions, which is stronger. Imam Fakhr al-Islam's apparent contradiction is resolved: he meant that ijma cannot abrogate the Book and Sunnah, but can abrogate other ijma. The discussion then turns to consensus based on inspiration: if it's allowed, it could abrogate even the Quran and Sunnah, but this would nullify the seal of prophethood, so it's rejected. The final argument from those who allow abrogation of ijma: if the ummah differed on two opinions, then they agree it's ijtihad, but if they later reach consensus on one, the permissibility of the other is removed, implying abrogation of the earlier ijma? The passage is incomplete but suggests this. The author presents all views with Hanafi leaning towards the majority position, with the nuance that change of maslaha can lead to abrogation of later ijma (non- Companion) by another ijma.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah on a ruling after the Prophet's time.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation: removal of a ruling by a later evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position presented, what condition allows a later consensus to abrogate an earlier consensus?
A) The earlier consensus was based on a solitary hadith.
B) The earlier consensus was a Companion consensus.
C) The earlier consensus is non-Companion and there is a change in maslaha.
D) Consensus can never be abrogated under any condition.

Key Takeaway
Ijma is generally non-abrogable, but non-Companion consensus may be overridden by a later consensus if maslaha changes, provided it does not involve definitive textual proofs.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
12 min
Refuting the Claim that Ijma' Can Abrogate (Naskh)
Detailed rebuttal of arguments for ijma' as a source of naskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that ijma' cannot abrogate (naskh) and evaluate the counterarguments from those who claim it can.

Core Idea
Ijma' indicates abrogation but is not the abrogator itself; only divine texts can abrogate.

In this passage, the commentator systematically dismantles the argument that ijma' (consensus) can serve as a nasikh (abrogator). He presents four logical objections and then refutes the two historical proofs often cited: Uthman's ruling on inheritance and the Companions' dropping of the mu'allafat al-qulub share. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to distinguish between genuine abrogation (naskh) and mere termination of a ruling due to the end of its cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Determine the precise dispute: Can ijma' (consensus) be a nasikh (abrogator) that removes a previous ruling?
The opponents are those who cite historical instances to support abrogation by consensus.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that ijma' is not an independent abrogator. It either indicates an earlier abrogating text or clarifies a silent area; it does not overrule a clear divine text.
This distinction is crucial: ijma' can be evidence for abrogation but is not the cause.
3
Examine the four logical objections
The author presents four objections: (1) the text underlying ijma' may not be known to be later; (2) naskh does not entail error in consensus; (3) decisive and probable proofs do not conflict; (4) accepting ijma' as abrogator would allow ahad to abrogate mutawatir, which is impossible.
These objections show that the mechanism of naskh does not fit with the nature of consensus.
4
Analyze the two historical counterexamples
The opponents cite Uthman's statement about the mother's share and the dropping of mu'allafat al-qulub. The author explains that the first is a metaphorical interpretation (bayan) and the second is termination of a cause (intiha').
Neither involves legislative abrogation; they are clarifications or natural expiry.
5
Evaluate the final truth
The author concludes that any abrogating consensus must be based on a textual basis or divine inspiration that does not contradict the Sharia. Ijma' itself is not the abrogator.
This upholds the principle that only divine revelation can abrogate, preserving the finality of the Sharia.

Discoverer of the first principle/Book because it is decisive in clarifying the ruling, so ponder. (And) secondly (that perhaps the text) relied upon (is not known to be later, so it is not fit to be an abrogator, unlike consensus) which is known to be later. Then we do not accept that if it is based on a text, it is the abrogator; the response is clear: lack of knowledge of lateness only entails lack of knowledge of abrogation, not its actual lateness or its fitness as an abrogator. So if consensus is reached upon it, it must not be abrogated, otherwise consensus would be upon an abrogated ruling, which would be an error. Thus its lateness and abrogation are necessitated. Consensus is only [an indicator of] lateness and abrogation, not that it is an abrogator. Understand. (And) thirdly (that abrogation does not entail error) in consensus (just as with two mutawatir texts) one may abrogate the other without error in either. So then we do not accept that if the abrogated is decisive, consensus is an error; rather it is a decisive [proof] that raises the first decisive [proof]. (And) fourthly, it entails the impermissibility of abrogating ahad by mutawatir, because ahad falls short of mutawatir, so there is no conflict, hence no abrogation as you [opponents] said in the last part of the second dichotomy. (I say: if the first part is dropped and it is said): If consensus were an abrogator, then (first) the abrogated is either decisive or probable... (that would suffice) for the objective. (Then the first two objections are repelled) because they were based on his statement that if it is based on a text it is the abrogator, not consensus, and that [part] is removed. Then the two mutually abrogating [texts] are two proofs (that conflict if their times are the same—i.e., the time of the two conflicting proofs—and the decisive and probable do not conflict, so there is no abrogation between them). Consensus, since it is decisive, does not abrogate the probable, and abrogation of ahad by mutawatir (as mentioned) is only in the sense of non-continuation in his view. In it [there is a problem]: if this were the meaning, then restricting [the case] to ahad being earlier would have no benefit; rather mutawatir is an abrogator in this sense whether earlier or later. But the truth is that the two mutually abrogating [texts] must have the earlier one binding and effecting the legal ruling were it not for the later [one], and the earlier probable [text] likewise, for it is a legal ruling—even if probable—binding until the later [text] comes. And if it is accepted that conflict is necessary between the two mutually abrogating [texts], then the meaning is that they must be such that, were it not for a temporary obstacle, they would conflict. And if the earlier [proof] is a [solitary] report, then it is such that if the solitary reporter had not reported it, it and the decisive [proof] would conflict, so understand. Likewise, consensus disappears in the time of the existence of the decisive [proof], because there is no scope for anyone's opinion or fatwa in the presence of a mutawatir [text], so consensus does not conflict with it. (So there is no abrogation then; the last two [objections] are repelled—the third by the last, and the fourth by the first—understand.) But there is apparent objection: regarding the response to the fourth, you have understood; and regarding the response to the third, we do not accept that consensus disappears in the time of the decisive [proof], nor that there is no scope for opinion when combined with other opinions. Even if one opinion has no scope, how [can it be denied] when combined opinions are a decisive proof like a decisive text? Understand. And if consensus were permitted from inspiration without a basis, this prohibition would be extremely forceful. Understand. The truth in the deduction is that the abrogating consensus, if based on a basis, is established from the noble era, so the abrogator is [that basis]. And if it is from inspiration, then this inspiration does not contradict what is established in the radiant Sharia. For the Muhammadan Sharia has left no benefit without bringing its ruling, and this benefit and ruling do not change, and Allah is pleased with it. To forbid it is obstinacy that no one with manners regarding the Muhammadan seal would heed. Understand, O those who permit the abrogative nature of consensus. (They said, first): When Ibn Abbas asked, Allah said: {If he has brothers, then for his mother the sixth} [Quran 4:11], but you reduce the mother from a third to a sixth with two brothers, even though they are not [real] brothers? (The Commander of the Faithful, Uthman, replied): 'Your people have prevented her, O boy, meaning from the third to the sixth with two brothers, and its derivation has passed; thus the people abrogated the Book by their consensus.' (We say, first): The verse is silent about the case of the mother with two brothers, and the Commander of the Faithful reduced her in this case from a third to a sixth. Ibn Abbas asked because the verse does not cover it, so the Commander of the Faithful used consensus in what the Book was silent about. This is not abrogation at all, and it is very clear. (We say, second): (Its meaning) i.e., the meaning of the Commander of the Faithful's statement 'brothers' (is metaphorical) for 'more than one' (by consensus), and (this metaphorical usage) is not abrogation by consensus, so it is not from the topic at all. (And we say, third): If it is granted that the people abrogated [based] on what appeared to them of evidence, and that evidence is the real abrogator, then (consensus) is a proof of the abrogator, like the Companion's action contrary to an explicit text is a proof of the abrogator. Understand. (And they said, second): The share of the mu'allafat al-qulub (those whose hearts are to be reconciled) was dropped (by consensus of the Companions in the time of the Caliph of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. Al-Tabarani narrated from Umar: When Uyaynah ibn Hisn came to him, he said: {The truth is from your Lord, so let whosoever will believe, and let whosoever will disbelieve} [Quran 18:29], meaning today there is no [need for] mu'allafah, and no Companion denied it, so it became a consensus. Thus in al-Taysir.) (We say): This is (of the type of termination of a ruling due to the termination of its cause) known to the Companions through prophetic indications. The expression 'mu'allafat al-qulub' also indicates that, for they were only given to strengthen the religion through them, and now it has become strong without their help, to the extent that it is said: strengthening now lies in not giving to them. This is clear. (And this), i.e., termination of a ruling due to termination of its cause, (is not called abrogation, because it is a clear termination) known before the existence of what is imagined to be an abrogator; rather the ruling is temporally conditioned by it. So what [they claim] that every abrogation is like that, i.e., termination of a ruling due to termination of its cause, is false because it is impossible for the cause to remain [while the ruling is elevated]. And it may also be imagined that just as they knew the termination of the ruling in this case, they could know in another case after some time the negation of the cause, so they would rule on the termination of the ruling, which is abrogation by consensus. Pay no attention to it, for we have explained that Allah has perfected the Muhammadan Sharia to the extent that no ruling remains to be revealed after him—prayers and peace be upon him and his family and Companions. So no termination of a ruling is known except by being informed by revelation—prayers of Allah be upon him and his family and Companions and peace—and no Muslim dares to deny this. The greatest Shaykh (may his secret be sanctified) has explained this in numerous places in his noble books.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an extensive usul dispute on whether ijma' (consensus) can serve as a nasikh (abrogator) of previous rulings. The commentator, addressing those who claim ijma' can abrogate, presents a series of rebuttals. First, he argues that a text relied upon for ijma' may not be known to be later than the ruling it supposedly abrogates, so it cannot be a valid abrogator, whereas ijma' itself is known to be later, but that only indicates the abrogation, not that ijma' is the abrogator. Second, abrogation does not entail error; just as two mutawatir texts can abrogate one another without error, so can a decisive ruling be raised by another decisive proof, and consensus is decisive. Third, accepting ijma' as an abrogator would imply that a singular (ahad) report cannot abrogate a mutawatir, but the author says that ahad and mutawatir do not conflict, so no abrogation occurs. Fourthly, the objection that ijma' as an abrogator leads to the impossibility of abrogating ahad by mutawatir is addressed. The author then refutes the two main proofs of the proponents: the incident of Uthman and Ibn Abbas regarding inheritance with two brothers, and the dropping of the share of mu'allafat al-qulub by consensus. For the first, the commentator explains that the verse is silent about the specific case, so Uthman's use of ijma' was to clarify the silent area, not to abrogate. For the second, he argues that it was a termination of the ruling due to the termination of its cause ('illah)—the need to strengthen Islam—not a legislative abrogation. The core point is that ijma' cannot introduce a new ruling overruling an established text; rather, it either indicates an existing abrogator or clarifies the scope of a text.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijmāʿ): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah on a religious matter after the death of the Prophet.
النسخ (al-naskh): The abrogation of a former ruling by a later one, where both rulings are from divine sources.
الناسخ (al-nāsikh): The abrogating proof that removes a previous ruling.
المنسوخ (al-mansūkh): The earlier ruling that is abrogated and no longer applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in the passage, why is the dropping of the mu'allafat al-qulub share not considered naskh?
A) Because the Companions did not reach consensus.
B) Because the ruling was only temporary and the cause ended.
C) Because the Quranic verse was abrogated by another verse.
D) Because the share was never obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a proof (hujjah) but not an abrogator (nasikh); it only indicates an existing abrogator or clarifies a silent area.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
12 min
Conditions of Tawatur and Ibn al-Hajib's Objection
Defines conditions of tawatur and defends against critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a report to be mutawatir according to the Hanafi school and evaluate Ibn al-Hajib's objection to the fourth condition by applying the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Tawatur yields certainty by custom, not logical necessity; its four conditions guard against error.

The concept of tawatur is foundational in Usul al-Fiqh: it determines when a report is certain (‘ilm yaqīnī) versus speculative (ẓannī). The Hanafīs delineate four conditions without which a report cannot be mutawatir. This passage explains those conditions and defends them against the objection of Ibn al-Hajib, who argued that the fourth condition is redundant. You will learn not only the conditions but also the underlying rationale that certainty from tawatur is based on customary human behavior (ʿādah) rather than logical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
From the passage, list the four conditions for tawatur: (1) multiplicity preventing collusion customarily, (2) reliance on the senses, (3) equality of all layers in number, (4) narrators being certain (not conjecturers).
The number of narrators is not fixed; it's the impossibility of collusion.
2
Understand the epistemological basis
Note that certainty from tawatur is by custom (bil-ʿādah), not by logical necessity (lā lizām ʿaqlī). This means it relies on human nature, not absolute proof.
This Hanafi position distinguishes them from some Mu'tazilites who demanded logical proof.
3
Follow Ibn al-Hajib's objection
Ibn al-Hajib argued that the fourth condition (narrators' certainty) is either false (if meant for all) or entailed by the first three conditions (if meant for some).
He claimed the first three conditions already imply that some narrators must be certain.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response clarifies that the first condition only requires a certain number in one layer, not in all layers. The third condition separately requires equality of layers. Thus, the first does not entail the fourth. Moreover, reliance on senses does not guarantee narrators' own certainty.
The text adds a third possibility: the group that constitutes the number in each layer does not entail that they are all certain.
5
Apply the distinction
Consider a report: if one condition is missing (e.g., the report is about an intellectual matter), it cannot be tawatur. Conversely, if all four are met, the report is certain and must be accepted.
For example, reports about the existence of Mecca are mutawatir; reports about philosophical doctrines are not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيفية الحصول فلم يختلف فيه والحل (أن الملازمة الأولى ممنوعة، فإن (بداهة البديهي يجوز أن تكون نظرية فإن البداهة صفة خارجة عن الشيء، فيجوز أن لا يعلم ثبوته إلا بالكسب والمراجعة إلى كيفية الحصول غير كافية فإنها قد تنسى بتطاول ،الزمان وكثرة الصور ووجود صورة الترتيب، هل كان هذا حاصلاً بالنظر وقد نسي، أو بالبديهة لا سيما في التصديقات، فإنه بعد البيان بالمقدمات يبقى العلم بالمطلوب ضرورة، فيقع الشك في أنه هل كان ههنا مقدمات نسيت أو لم تكن بل حصل ضرورة، وأما في التصورات فقد ناقش بعض المتأخرين، وقد بينا ما هو الحق في حواشينا على الحاشية الزاهدية المتعلقة بشرح المواقف ولو سلم) أن بداهة البديهي بديهية فلا تستلزم البداهة الوفاق لجواز الخفاء) فإنّ البديهي ربما يكون خفياً فيختلف فيه فلا نسلم الملازمة الثانية، ألم تر السوفسطائية كيف خالفوا في القضايا الضرورية ( فتدبر) ولا تزل فإنه مزلة .
(مسألة: للتواتر شروط ينتفي بانتفاء واحد منها فمن زعم نظريته) أي نظرية العلم به اشترط تقدم العلم بها ولعلهم زعموا أنها شروط يتوقف عليها اكتسابه كما يلوح من الدليل الأول لهم، ومن قال بالبداهة لا يشترط تقدم العلم ،البتة بل يقول : إن حدوث العلم به في نفس الأمر يتوقف على تحققها فيها فمنها تعدد المخبرين تعدداً يمنع التواطؤ على الكذب) لا عمداً ولا سهواً ولا نسياناً (عادة) وفي تعيين هذا العدد خلاف كما سنذكر إن شاء الله تعالى (ومنها الاستناد إلى الحس بأن أحس المخبرون الأولون بمضمون الخبر (فلا تواتر في العقليات فلا تقبل حماقة المشائين من الفلاسفة أن لا حشر للأجساد، وذلك لأن العقلي لو كان بديهياً فيفيد العلم بنفسه، فلا دخل فيه للمخبر، وإلا فيحتمل الخطأ، بل ربما يتيقن به كما في خبر المشائين الحمقى (ومنها استواء جميع الطبقات إن كان هناك طبقات (في مبلغ يفيد اليقين) فيجب أن يكون المخبرون الأولون جماعة يمتنع تواطؤهم على الكذب، وكذا كذلك المخبرون عنهم ثم وثم (ومنها كونهم (عالمين متيقنين لا ظانين ولا شاكين (بالمخبر عنه، إذ لا علم إلا عن علم ولقائل أن يقول : إن إفادة التواتر العلم بالعادة لا للزوم عقلي، فيجوز أن يكون إخبار الظانين يقوي ظن السامع بحيث يبلغ اليقين، فالأولى أن يحال إلى الضرورة، فإنا نعلم ضرورة أنه لو قال المخبرون : نحن غير مستيقنين بالخبر، ويحتمل عندنا أن لا يكون كذلك، لا يحصل العلم قطعياً، وإنكاره مكابرة (وقال الشيخ (ابن الحاجب : هذا الشرط مما لا يحتاج إليه، لأنه إن أريد علم الجميع من المخبرين (فباطل، لجواز أن يكون بعضهم ظانا فإنه إذا استيقن من المخبرين جماعة، وكان بعضهم ظاناً يفيد العلم قطعاً (وإن أريد البعض أي علم البعض منهم فهو لازم من القيود الثلاثة السابقة (عادة لأنها لا تجتمع) يمتنع تواطؤهم على الكذب (إلا) والبعض عالم به قطعاً فلا حاجة إلى هذا الشرط (أقول : أزيد) أنا (شقاً ثالثا هو الجمع الذي يحصل به عدد التواتر في كل طبقة ولزوم هذا من القيود الثلاثة المذكورة (ممنوع) فإن كون الجماعة عدداً لا يمكن تواطؤهم على الكذب في كل طبقة لا يلزم منه كونهم ،عالمين، وهو ظاهر جداً، فإن قلت الاستناد إلى الحسن مغن عنه، جماعة :
فإنهم إذا أخبروا بخبر بأنهم أحسوا به لزم علمهم قطعاً قلت المراد بالاستناد إلى الحس أن يكون الخبر في المحسوسات لا أنهم أخبروا بأنهم أحسوا فلا إغناء فتأمل، (قيل) في حواشي ميرزاجان لو كان اشتراط الملزوم مغنياً عن اشتراط اللازم) كما قال ابن الحاجب (أغنى اشتراط (الأول وهو بلوغ المخبرين عدداً يمتنع تواطؤهم على الكذب (عن الأخيرين) كونهم كذلك في كل طبقة، والاستناد إلى الحس لأنه إذا بلغ عدد المخبرين حداً يمنع العقل الاتفاق على الكذب لا يكون ذلك إلا في المحسوس فإن العقلي لا يمتنع فيه الاتفاق على الكذب ويلزم استواء الوسط والطرفين وإلا جاز الاتفاق، لكن إغناء اشتراط الملزوم عن اللازم ثابت فيلزم انتفاء اشتراط الأخيرين أو يقال : إن إغناء اشتراط الأول الأخيرين عن باطل، فيلزم بطلان إغناء اشتراط الملزوم عن اشتراط اللازم وحينئذ فيحتاج إلى الأخير وإن كان الأول مستلزماً إياه فعلى الأول إيراد على الجمهور مثل إيراد ابن الحاجب وعلى الثاني : جواب عن إيراد ابن الحاجب (أقول ) لا يصح هذا الكلام كيفما كان، بل (المراد من الشرط الأول وجود المبلغ في الحد المذكور (في طبقة ما من الطبقات (وأما) وجود هذا المبلغ (في جميع الطبقات فمن الشرط الثالث ولا شك في عدم لزوم هذا من الأول (والمراد بمنع العقل) التواطأ على الكذب ومنعه بعد وجود سائر الشرائط) يعني أن المراد منه اجتماع العدد من جهة الكثرة، ولو كان يحصل هذا المنع بعد تحقق شرائط أخرى، حتى لا يحتاج منع التواطؤ إلى عدد أزيد منه وليس المراد امتناع التواطؤ في الحال حتى يرد عليه أن ذلك متضمن لسائر الشرائط، فهو ملزوم لها (وحينئذ ظهر أن الأول ليس بملزوم للأخيرين هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم) هذا المقام
Concerning the manner of attainment, there is no disagreement, and the solution is that the first implication is denied: indeed the self-evidence of the self-evident may be theoretical, because self-evidence is an attribute external to the thing, so it is possible that its existence is not known except through acquisition and review. The manner of attainment is not sufficient, because it may be forgotten over time and with the abundance of forms and the existence of the form of arrangement: was this obtained by reasoning and then forgotten, or by intuition? Especially in affirmations, for after clarification by premises, knowledge of the sought remains necessary, so doubt occurs whether there were premises here that were forgotten or not, rather it came necessarily. As for concepts, some later scholars have discussed it, and we have shown what is correct in our glosses on the Hashiya Zâhidiyya related to the Sharh al-Mawâqif. And even if it is conceded that the self-evidence of the self-evident is self-evident, it does not entail self-evidence of agreement due to the possibility of hiddenness. For the self-evident may sometimes be hidden, so there is disagreement over it, thus we do not concede the second implication. Do you not see how the Sophists disagreed over necessary propositions? So reflect, and do not slip, for it is a slippery place.
(Issue: Tawatur has conditions, by the negation of any one of which it ceases. So whoever claims its theoretical nature, i.e., the theoretical nature of knowledge from it, requires prior knowledge of these conditions. Perhaps they claim that these conditions are prerequisites upon which its acquisition depends, as appears from their first proof. But whoever says it is intuitive does not require prior knowledge at all. Rather, he says: The occurrence of knowledge from it in reality depends on the realization of these conditions in it. Among them are: multiplicity of informants to a degree that prevents collusion in lying, whether intentionally, inadvertently, or forgetfully, customarily. There is disagreement on specifying this number, as we shall mention if Allah wills. Among them: reliance on the senses, in that the first informants sensed the content of the report; thus there is no tawatur in intellectual matters, so the foolishness of the Peripatetic philosophers that there is no resurrection of bodies is not accepted. That is because if the intellectual matter is intuitive, it gives knowledge by itself, so the reporter has no role; otherwise, error is possible. Rather, it may be certain, as in the report of the foolish Peripatetics. Among them: equality of all layers, if there are layers, in a number that yields certainty. Thus the first informants must be a group whose collusion in lying is impossible, and likewise those after them, and so on. Among them: that they be knowledgeable and certain, not conjecturers nor doubters, about the reported matter, because knowledge only comes from knowledge. But one may say: The acquisition of knowledge from tawatur is by custom, not by logical necessity, so it is possible that the report of conjecturers strengthens the conjecture of the listener to the point of reaching certainty. So it is better to refer to necessity, for we know necessarily that if the informants say, 'We are not certain of the report, and it is possible in our view that it is not so,' certain knowledge is not obtained, and denial of that is obstinacy. And Shaykh Ibn al-Hajib said: This condition is not needed, because if what is meant is knowledge of all the informants, it is false, for it is possible that some of them are conjecturers—if a group of informants are certain, and some are conjecturers, it gives certain knowledge. And if what is meant is the knowledge of some of them, then it is entailed by the previous three conditions customarily, because they do not come together except with some being certain of it, so this condition is unnecessary. I say: I add a third possibility: the group that constitutes the number of tawatur in each layer, and the entailment of this from the three mentioned conditions is denied, for the mere fact that a group is a number whose collusion in lying is impossible in each layer does not entail that they are certain—this is quite apparent. For if you say: Reliance on the sense makes it unnecessary. For if they report a report saying they sensed it, their knowledge becomes certain. I say: What is meant by reliance on the sense is that the report be about sense-perceptibles, not that they report that they sensed; thus it does not suffice—so reflect. It was said in the glosses of Mîrzâ Jân: If the conditioning of the entailed were sufficient instead of the conditioning of the entailer, as Ibn al-Hajib said, then the conditioning of the first—that the informants reach a number that prevents collusion in lying—would suffice instead of the last two: that they be such in every layer, and reliance on the sense, because when the number of informants reaches a limit that the mind prevents agreement on lying, that only happens in sense-perceptibles, for in intellectual matters agreement on lying is not prevented, and it necessitates equality of middle and ends, otherwise agreement would be possible. But the sufficiency of conditioning the entailer over the entailer is established, so the conditioning of the last two becomes unnecessary. Or it may be said: The sufficiency of conditioning the first over the last two is false, so the sufficiency of conditioning the entailer over the conditioning of the entailer is false. In that case, the last is needed even if the first entails it. So on the first view, it is an objection against the majority like Ibn al-Hajib's objection; on the second, it is a response to Ibn al-Hajib's objection. I say: This statement is not correct in any case. Rather, what is meant by the first condition is the existence of the required number in some layer, while its existence in all layers is from the third condition, and there is no doubt that this is not entailed by the first. And what is meant by 'the mind's prevention of collusion in lying' is its prevention after the existence of other conditions, i.e., the meaning is the coming together of the number in terms of multitude, even if this prevention occurs after the realization of other conditions, so that the prevention of collusion does not need a larger number than that. It does not mean prevention of collusion immediately, such that it would be objected that it includes other conditions, so it is their entailer. Then it becomes apparent that the first is not an entailer of the last two—thus it should be understood.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions of tawatur (mutawatir reports). It begins with a discussion on the nature of badihī (self-evident) knowledge, clarifying that even self-evident propositions may be theoretical upon analysis, and that tawatur knowledge is not necessarily self-evident. The author then lists the four conditions for a report to be mutawatir: (1) multiplicity of narrators to a degree that customarily prevents collusion in lying — note that this number is debated later; (2) the report must be based on sense perception (muhsasāt), not intellectual matters, so tawatur does not apply to rational claims; (3) each layer of narrators must be equally numerous in a number that yields certainty; (4) the narrators must be certain and not conjecturing or doubting. The commentary addresses Ibn al-Hajib's objection to the fourth condition, arguing that it is either unnecessary or entailed by the previous ones. The author refutes this by showing that the first condition does not entail the others and provides a detailed logical analysis of the relationship between the conditions. The discussion highlights the Hanafi view that tawatur yields certainty by custom (ādah), not logical necessity, and that the conditions are safeguards against error. The passage gives a nuanced defense of the classical position, engaging with critiques from Ibn al-Hajib and later scholars like Mīrzā Jān.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): A report conveyed by such a large number that collusion on falsehood is customarily impossible, producing certain knowledge
بديهي (badīhī): Self-evident; knowledge that arises without reasoning or acquisition
عادَة (ʿādah): Custom or habitual occurrence; the basis for the evidentiary value of tawātur according to Hanafīs, not logical necessity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the certainty produced by tawatur according to the Hanafi school in this passage?
A) Logical necessity (luzūm ʿaqlī)
B) Custom (ʿādah)
C) Divine guarantee
D) The large number alone

Key Takeaway
Tawatur requires four conditions: multiplicity preventing collusion, reliance on senses, equality of layers, and certainty of narrators; it yields certainty by custom, not logical necessity.
