The Condition of 'Adala for the Mujtahid in Ijma
Debate on the necessity of 'adala for the mujtahid in Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on 'adala for Ijma, state the opposing Shafi'i argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the source text.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school requires 'adala of the mujtahid for Ijma because the fasiq's word is unreliable and Ijma authority is honor-based.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut tackles a foundational usul dispute: Does the personal integrity ('adala) of the mujtahid affect the binding nature of Ijma? The Hanafis and majority condition 'adala, while leading Shafi'i scholars like al-Amidi and al-Ghazali reject the condition. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to evaluate how usul principles—like the scope of general proofs—translate into differing rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the core question: Is 'adala of each mujtahid a condition for Ijma to be authoritative? Then clearly state: Hanafis (and majority) say yes; Shafi'is (al-Amidi, al-Ghazali) say no.
The passage labels the Shafi'i view as 'the chosen opinion' of those two scholars.
2
Extract the Shafi'i dalil
The Shafi'i argument: The proofs establishing the authority of Ijma (e.g., 'Follow the way of the believers') are unrestricted (mutlaqa) and do not restrict the Umma to upright individuals. Therefore, no condition of 'adala can be added without a textual basis.
This is a classic usul move: the unrestricted text leaves no room for additional conditions.
3
Extract the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafis counter: (1) The statement of a fasiq is to be suspended (wajib al-tawaqquf) in worldly matters, so how can it be authoritative in religion? (2) The authority of Ijma is essentially for honoring its people (takrim), and the fasiq does not deserve honour.
Note the dual basis: epistemic (unreliability) and teleological (honour).
4
Analyze the counterarguments
The text presents a possible objection: perhaps honour (takrim) is a consequence of authority, not its basis. The Hanafis respond that even if honour is a consequence, it still cannot be applied to the fasiq. Another objection: the fasiq may be honourable because he will ultimately enter Paradise. The Hanafis rebut this by noting that in this world his statement is not accepted, so he is not honourable in terms of his opinion.
The text also mentions the exception of the openly sinful (mu'lin) and hadiths on concealment, but the Hanafi response remains firm.
5
Summarize the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that 'adala is required because the fasiq's word is unreliable and authority entails honour. The Shafi'i unrestricted dalil is restricted (takhsis) by these considerations. Hence, Ijma of non-'udul is not binding.
This is the mu'tamad (reliable) view in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: لا يشترط عدالة المجتهد في الإجماع فيتوقف على غير العدل في مختار الآمدي و الإمام حجة الإسلام الغزالي قدس سره، كلاهما من الشافعية (لأن الأدلة الدالة على حجية الإجماع (مطلقة) عن تقييد الأمة بكونها عدلاً، فاعتبار إجماع العدول الفاسق لا مدرك له شرعاً وكل حكم لا مدرك له شرعاً وجب نفيه وهذا إنما يتم إذا كان الأمة المطلقة شاملة للفساق في العرف القديم والحنفية بل الجمهور شرطوا العدالة) وهو الحق لأن قول الفاسق واجب التوقف فلا دخل له في الحجية ولأن (الحجية) في الاجماع (حقيقة للتكريم لأهله، والفاسق لا يستحق التكريم، وقد يقال : لم يدل دليل على أن الحجية للتكريم، وإنما اللازم أن التكريم ثبت بالحجية، وأين هذا من ذاك؟ وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنا قد أشرنا سابقاً في تقرير بعض الحجج السمعية أنها للتكريم مع أنه يكفي لنا كون الحجية مستلزمة له، فنقول : لو كان قولهم معتبراً في الحجية لزم تكريمهم ، وهو منتف أيضاً (وقد يقال إنه أهل له أي للتكريم لدخول الجنة فإن المؤمن لا يخلد في النار فيتوقف الإجماع عليه، كذا نقل عن الإمام شمس الأئمة، إلا أنه استثنى الفاسق المعلن ولا يخفى عليك أن الحجية لا توجب التقيد بالإعلان في عدم القبول اللهم إلا أن يقال إنه ورد في بعض الأحاديث الوعد بالمغفرة لمن ستر ذنوبه، والوعيد الشديد على من فضحه الله تعالى في الدنيا، وهذا يعطي الظن بالمغفرة لمن ستر ذنوبه وفسقه بخلاف المعلن على الشك فتأمل فيه ويدفع بأنه لم يعتبر) قوله (في الدنيا بدليل وجوب التوقف في اخباره فلا يكون أهلاً للتكريم باعتبار قوله،
Issue: The 'adala (integrity) of the mujtahid is not a condition in Ijma, according to the chosen opinion of al-Amidi and Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali (may Allah sanctify their spirits), both from the Shafi'is. Because the evidences proving the authority of Ijma are unrestricted (mutlaqa) without restricting the Umma to being 'adl. So considering the consensus of the upright and excluding the corrupt has no basis in Shari'a, and any ruling with no basis must be negated. This is only valid if the unrestricted 'Umma' includes the corrupt in the ancient custom. And the Hanafis, rather the majority, have conditioned 'adala. And it is the truth because the statement of the corrupt (fasiq) is to be suspended, so it has no role in authority. And because authority in Ijma is essentially for honoring its people, and the corrupt does not deserve honor. It might be said that no evidence indicates that authority is for honor; rather, honor is established by authority. But we previously indicated in establishing some of the scriptural proofs that it is for honor. And it is sufficient for us that authority entails honor. So we say: if their statement were considered in authority, then honoring them would be necessary, which is also not the case. And it might be said that he (the fasiq) is deserving of honor because he will enter Paradise, for the believer will not abide eternally in Hellfire, so Ijma is dependent on him. This is transmitted from Imam Shams al-A'imma, except he excluded the openly corrupt (al-mu'lin). And it is not hidden from you that authority does not necessitate restriction by publicity in non-acceptance, unless it is said that there are some hadiths promising forgiveness for those who hide their sins and severe warning for those whom Allah exposes in this world, which gives the presumption of forgiveness for the one who hides his sins and corruption, unlike the one who is open in sin. So reflect on it. And it is rebutted: because his statement is not considered in this world, as evidenced by the obligation to suspend accepting his reports, so he is not deserving of honor in terms of his statement.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage discusses a key dispute: Should the mujtahid be 'adl (upright and just) for his opinion to count in Ijma? The Shafi'i scholars al-Amidi and al-Ghazali argue no, because the general proofs of Ijma do not restrict the Umma to only righteous people. The Hanafis and the majority require 'adala, because the word of a fasiq is not reliable and Ijma's authority is tied to honor (takrim) which the fasiq does not deserve. The text also discusses the exception of the openly sinful (mu'lin) and the counterargument that the fasiq may still be honorable because he will eventually enter Paradise. However, the Hanafi response is that his statement is not accepted in worldly matters, so he is not worthy of honor.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adala): Moral integrity and uprightness that makes one reliable in testimony and report.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the fasiq is not a Muslim.
B) Because the word of a fasiq is not trustworthy and Ijma's authority is based on honor.
C) Because only the righteous can be mujtahids.
D) Because the Quran explicitly requires 'adala.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires 'adala of the mujtahid for Ijma because the fasiq's word is unreliable and Ijma authority is honor-based.

Authority of Later Ijma and Following Earlier Mujtahids
Analyzing an objection about fatwa without evidence and the role of ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the authority of later ijma over earlier ijtihad and apply the Hanafi position on a muqallid following a previous mujtahid despite later consensus.

Core Idea
Later ijma does not automatically override earlier ijtihad; a muqallid may follow a previous mujtahid's opinion.

This lesson examines a key debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: can a later consensus (ijma) erase the validity of an earlier mujtahid's ruling? The source passage refutes the claim that any fatwa without evidence is haram and clarifies that a muqallid (lay follower) may adhere to an earlier opinion even after later scholars have agreed on the opposite. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the limits of ijma and the nature of taqlid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its basis
The objection claims that giving a fatwa without evidence is clearly haram by nass, and that later ijma indicates a decisive proof, so opposing it is opposing the decisive.
The objector equates ijma with qati' evidence.
2
Analyze the Hanafi refutation regarding zanni proofs
The Hanafi response argues that the basis of ijma may be speculatively (zanni) clear, so the claim that agreement indicates a decisive proof is denied.
This introduces the crucial usul principle: not all consensus is based on qati' dalil.
3
Distinguish between ijma of Companions and later ijma
The passage restricts the absolute prohibition to ijma of the Companions. For later ijma, after disagreements have been recorded, there is room for discussion.
Later ijma does not automatically nullify earlier ijtihad.
4
Examine the muqallid's position
If a muqallid opposes later ijma by following an earlier mujtahid, it is permissible because he is not using his own opinion but adhering to a previous scholarly opinion.
The act of taqlid is valid even if it appears to contradict later consensus.
5
Derive the practical ruling
The key practical result: a muqallid may follow any earlier mujtahid, and later ijma does not make that forbidden as long as the muqallid is not relying on his own opinion.
This preserves the diversity of ijtihad in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فافهم (وقد يعترض بأن من قال باعتباره يمنع الحرمة ولعل هذا مكابرة، فإنه من الظاهر أنه أفتى لا عن دليل وهو حرام بالنص وما في شرح الشرح) لدفعه أن اتفاق المجتهدين يدل على وجود قاطع دال على الحكم، فمخالفته مخالفة القاطع وهو حرام (فمدفوع بأن مستند الإجماع ربما يكون ظنياً جلياً فدلالة الاتفاق على القاطع ممنوعة والأولى كما قيل) في حواشي میرزاجان» (اتفاقهم من حيث هم مجتهدون لا يكون إلا برأيهم قطعاً (ولا شك أن مخالفته للمجتهد برأيه (حرام إذ ليس له رأي معتبر شرعاً فتدبر) بقي أن هذا إنما يتم في إجماع الصحابة، وأما اجماع من بعدهم بعد تقرر الخلاف فللمناقشة فيه مجال، لأن مخالفة بعدهم مع موافقة واحد ممن قبلهم ليس حراماً عليه فإن المقلد له أن يقلد قول أي مجتهد شاء، فإن قلت فيه مخالفة الإجماع، لأنه قد أمات الأقوال السابقة فيحرم مخالفته، قلت: كونه إجماعاً هو أول المسألة، هذا لكن الحق غير خاف على من له أدنى تدبر فإن مخالفة هذا المقلد لمجتهدي زمانه إن كان بالرأي فهو حرام غير ناشيء عن الدليل الشرعي فلا اعتداد به، وإن كان لكونه موافقاً لقول مجتهد سابق عليهم فاعتبار قوله لأنه قول مجتهد سابق بالحقيقة فهو اعتبار لقول ذلك المجتهد فقد آل إلى أن الإجماع اللاحق هل هو حجة مخالفة المجتهد السابق أم لا؟ وسيجيء ولا دخل لمخالفة المقلد ومما ذكرنا ظهر اندفاع ما في «الحاشية» أنه يجوز أن يكون لمجتهد قولان ووقع الاتفاق على أحدهما، والمقلد يجوز أن يقلد الأول فلا حرمة، فيجوز أن يعتبر فتأمل .
So understand. It may be objected that whoever holds that it is permissible (to follow a mujtahid's opinion) prevents prohibition, and perhaps this is arrogant. For it is apparent that he gave a fatwa without evidence, and that is prohibited by the text. And what is in Sharh al-Sharh to refute it is that the agreement of the mujtahids indicates the existence of a decisive proof indicating the ruling, so opposing it is opposing the decisive, which is prohibited. But it is refuted that the basis of ijma may be clearly speculative, so the indication of agreement on the decisive is denied. The better view, as it is said in the glosses of Mirzajan, is that their agreement insofar as they are mujtahids is only by their own opinion decisively, and there is no doubt that opposing the mujtahid in his opinion is prohibited, since he has no legally valid opinion, so reflect. What remains is that this applies only to the ijma of the Companions. As for ijma after them after the establishment of disagreement, there is room for discussion, because opposing them while agreeing with one from those before them is not prohibited for him, for the muqallid may follow the opinion of any mujtahid he wishes. If you say: in it is opposition to ijma because he has neglected the previous opinions, so opposing it is prohibited. I say: its being ijma is the first point of the issue. But the truth is not hidden from anyone with minimal reflection: the opposition of this muqallid to the mujtahids of his time, if it is by opinion, is prohibited, not arising from legal evidence, so it is not considered. But if it is because he agrees with the opinion of a previous mujtahid, then his saying is considered because it is the saying of a previous mujtahid in reality, so it is a consideration of that mujtahid's saying. So it reduces to whether the later ijma is a proof opposing the earlier mujtahid or not? And it will come later. And the opposition of the muqallid has no relevance. From what we have mentioned, the refutation of what is in al-Hashiya becomes apparent: that it is permissible for a mujtahid to have two opinions and agreement occurred on one of them, and the muqallid may follow the first, so there is no prohibition. So it is permissible to consider it, so reflect.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a polemical discussion within a commentary on a text about the authority of ijma. The author begins by presenting an objection: someone who claims that a mujtahid's opinion (even if without evidence) prevents prohibition is being arrogant, because giving a fatwa without evidence is clearly haram by nass. The objection attempts to defend that the agreement of mujtahids indicates a decisive proof, so opposing it is opposing the decisive. The author refutes this by saying that the basis of ijma may be clearly speculative (zanni), so the claim that agreement indicates a decisive proof is denied. He then cites a gloss by Mirzajan that the agreement of mujtahids as such is only by their own opinion decisively, and opposing a mujtahid in his own opinion is haram, since he has no legally valid opinion (i.e., his opinion is not authoritative for others). The author then clarifies that this ruling applies only to the ijma of the Companions. For later ijma after disagreements have been recorded, there is room for discussion. A muqallid who follows one earlier mujtahid against the later ijma is not necessarily opposing ijma, because the later ijma's authority over earlier ijtihad is questionable. The author explains that if the muqallid's opposition is based on his own opinion, it is haram because it is not based on evidence. But if he is following a previous mujtahid, then he is actually following that mujtahid's opinion, not his own, so it is permissible. He then refutes a point from 'al-Hashiya' that a mujtahid may have two opinions and agreement on one, and the muqallid may follow the other, so no prohibition. The author concludes that this is valid. Overall, the passage clarifies the limits of ijma's authority and the permissibility of following earlier opinions despite later consensus.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of mujtahids on a legal ruling.
مقلد (muqallid): A layperson who follows a mujtahid's opinion without independent reasoning.
قاطع (qati'): A definitive proof or evidence that yields certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it prohibited for a muqallid to oppose later ijma?
A) When the later ijma is based on a qati' proof.
B) When the muqallid uses his own opinion (ra'y) to oppose.
C) When the later ijma is from the time of the Companions.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid may legitimately follow an earlier mujtahid's opinion even after a later consensus, as long as he is not relying on his own opinion.

The Required 'Adala for Ijma Participants: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Stating the condition of 'adala for mujtahids in ijma and the dispute about including sinful scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that 'adala is required for ijma participants and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A fasiq's opinion is suspended — he cannot be counted in ijma because ijma requires honor.

This passage addresses a critical condition for the validity of ijma: the moral probity ('adala) of the participants. The Hanafi school, along with the majority, insists that only just individuals count toward consensus. Some Shafi'i scholars, however, argue that the proofs for ijma are absolute and include all members of the community. Let us examine the arguments and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested condition
Determine whether 'adala (justice) is a requirement for a mujtahid to be counted in ijma.
The dispute is between Hanafis and some Shafi'is.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafis require 'adala because the saying of a fasiq is suspended (mawquf) and ijma involves honor (takrim), which a sinner does not deserve.
The text explicitly says: 'قول الفاسق واجب التوقف فلا دخل له في الحجية ولأن الحجية في الاجماع حقيقة للتكريم لأهله، والفاسق لا يستحق التكريم'.
3
State the opposing Shafi'i position and its proof
Al-Amidi and al-Ghazali do not require 'adala because the proofs indicating the authority of ijma are absolute and not restricted to just individuals.
Their argument: 'الأدلة الدالة على حجية الإجماع مطلقة عن تقييد الأمة بكونها عدلاً'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The absolute term is restricted by other evidence; also, the concept of honor is inherent in authority, so a fasiq cannot contribute to honor.
The text refutes the Shafi'i claim and affirms the Hanafi view as the truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: لا يشترط عدالة المجتهد في الإجماع فيتوقف على غير العدل في مختار الآمدي و الإمام حجة الإسلام الغزالي قدس سره، كلاهما من الشافعية (لأن الأدلة الدالة على حجية الإجماع (مطلقة) عن تقييد الأمة بكونها عدلاً، فاعتبار إجماع العدول الفاسق لا مدرك له شرعاً وكل حكم لا مدرك له شرعاً وجب نفيه وهذا إنما يتم إذا كان الأمة المطلقة شاملة للفساق في العرف القديم والحنفية بل الجمهور شرطوا العدالة) وهو الحق لأن قول الفاسق واجب التوقف فلا دخل له في الحجية ولأن (الحجية) في الاجماع (حقيقة للتكريم لأهله، والفاسق لا يستحق التكريم، وقد يقال : لم يدل دليل على أن الحجية للتكريم، وإنما اللازم أن التكريم ثبت بالحجية، وأين هذا من ذاك؟ وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنا قد أشرنا سابقاً في تقرير بعض الحجج السمعية أنها للتكريم مع أنه يكفي لنا كون الحجية مستلزمة له، فنقول : لو كان قولهم معتبراً في الحجية لزم تكريمهم ، وهو منتف أيضاً (وقد يقال إنه أهل له أي للتكريم لدخول الجنة فإن المؤمن لا يخلد في النار فيتوقف الإجماع عليه، كذا نقل عن الإمام شمس الأئمة، إلا أنه استثنى الفاسق المعلن ولا يخفى عليك أن الحجية لا توجب التقيد بالإعلان في عدم القبول اللهم إلا أن يقال إنه ورد في بعض الأحاديث الوعد بالمغفرة لمن ستر ذنوبه، والوعيد الشديد على من فضحه الله تعالى في الدنيا، وهذا يعطي الظن بالمغفرة لمن ستر ذنوبه وفسقه بخلاف المعلن على الشك فتأمل فيه ويدفع بأنه لم يعتبر) قوله (في الدنيا بدليل وجوب التوقف في اخباره فلا يكون أهلاً للتكريم باعتبار قوله، كذا (لأنه المفسقة) ٢٦٩ الأصل الثالث الإجماع وهذا لا ينافي التكريم في الآخرة بوجه بعد إذلالهم وقيل : يعتبر قوله في حق نفسه فقط) فلا يعتبر الإجماع مع مخالفته في حقه ويعتبر في حق غيره (كالإقرار ) فإنه حجة في حقه دون غيره ويدفع بأنه قبل مخالفته كان نافعاً (له) لتكريمه (وإنما يقبل فيما عليه لا فيما له إجماعاً في شرح المختصر، أقول كل ما أدى إليه إجتهاده فيما لا (قاطع) فيه (فهو عليه إجماعاً) يجب عليه العمل به أولاً ولو كان له بالآخرة للتكريم فتدبر، واشتراط عدم البدعة وهي البدعة الجلية كالتجسيم والرفض والخروج ( كالعدالة) فمن شرطها وهم الجمهور والحنفية قاطبة يشترط عدم البدعة أيضاً، ومن لا ،فلا والأول هو الصحيح، كيف لا وأنه قد غلب مكابرة الهوى على العقل وانغمص رأيهم في تعصبهم، فوقعوا في ضلالة وظلمة، فيريهم الهوى خلاف ما هو عليه فلا اعتداد بهم واعتبار القول في الإجماع إنما كان لجامع صحة الرأي فإن قلت ما بال أكثر الشافعية حيث قبلوا رواية المبتدع الذي يرى الكذب حراماً ولا يدخلونهم في الإجماع وما الفرق قلت لعل الفرق عندهم أن مذهبهم أوقعهم فيما أوقعهم ومع ذلك يحرمون الكذب فلا يجترؤون عليه وعدم قبول الرواية كان لريبة الكذب لا غير، وأما الدخول في الإجماع فإنما هو بالرأي، وقد أفسدوه لاختيار مكابرة الهوى على العقل، ونحن قد بينا عدم قبول روايتهم أيضاً، ثم إنه إذا تأملت فيما ألقينا ظهر لك أنهم أجدر بعدم الاعتبار من الفاسق فإن الفاسق ما أفسد رأيه، بل أهدر قوله شرعاً فافهم.
Issue: The justice of the mujtahid is not required in ijma, so it is based on the non-just person according to the chosen view of al-Amidi and Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, may their secrets be sanctified, both from the Shafi'is, because the proofs indicating the authority of ijma are absolute, not restricted to the ummah being just. So considering the ijma of the just and the sinful has no legal basis, and every ruling with no legal basis must be negated. This only holds if the absolute term 'ummah' includes the sinful in ancient custom. The Hanafis, indeed the majority, conditioned justice. And it is the truth, because the saying of a sinful person must be suspended, so he has no role in authority. And because authority in ijma is in reality for honoring its people, and the sinful does not deserve honor. It may be said: No evidence indicates that authority is for honoring; rather, honor is established by authority. Where is this from that? And you are not unaware that we previously indicated in establishing some scriptural proofs that it is for honoring, while it suffices for us that authority entails it. So we say: If their saying were considered in authority, it would necessitate honoring them, which is also negated. It may be said that he is deserving of it, i.e., honor, because of entry into Paradise, for the believer does not remain eternally in Hell. So ijma depends on him. Thus it is transmitted from Imam Shams al-A'imma, except that he excluded the open sinner. And it is not hidden from you that authority does not necessitate restriction by publicity regarding non-acceptance, unless it is said that some hadiths promise forgiveness for one who conceals his sins, and severe threat for one whom Allah exposes in this world. This gives the conjecture of forgiveness for one who conceals his sins and corruption, unlike the open one, who is in doubt. So reflect on it. And it is refuted that he is not considered because of the obligation to suspend judgment on his reports, so he is not deserving of honor by virtue of his saying. So (because it is corrupt?) The third principle: ijma. And this does not contradict honor in the Hereafter at all after their humiliation. And it is said: His saying is considered only in his own right. So ijma is not considered with his opposition regarding him, but it is considered regarding others, like confession. For it is proof regarding him but not others. And it is refuted that before his opposition it was beneficial for him for his honor, and it is accepted in what is against him, not for him by ijma in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. I say: Everything his ijtihad leads to in matters where there is no decisive proof, it is upon him by ijma. He must act on it initially, even if it is for him in the Hereafter for honor, so reflect. And the condition of avoiding innovation, which is clear innovation like anthropomorphism, rejection, and secession, is like justice. So whoever conditions justice, the majority and all Hanafis also condition avoidance of innovation. And whoever does not, does not. The first is correct. How not? For the arrogance of desire has overcome reason, and their opinion has sunk in their fanaticism, so they fall into error and darkness. Desire shows them other than what is true, so they are not considered. And consideration of saying in ijma is only for the collection of sound opinion. If you say: Why do most Shafi'is accept the narration of an innovator who considers lying forbidden but do not include him in ijma? What is the difference? I say: Perhaps the difference with them is that their school has placed them where they have, and yet they forbid lying, so they do not dare to do it. Non-acceptance of narration was only due to suspicion of lying, nothing else. As for inclusion in ijma, it is by opinion, and they have corrupted it by choosing the arrogance of desire over reason. And we have already shown non-acceptance of their narration as well. Then if you reflect on what we have presented, it becomes clear that they are more deserving of non-consideration than the sinful. For the sinful did not corrupt his opinion, but his saying is disregarded legally. So understand.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition of 'adala (justice) for a mujtahid to be counted in ijma. The text first presents the view of some Shafi'is (al-Amidi and al-Ghazali) that justice is not required because the proofs of ijma are absolute. The Hanafi position, along with the majority, conditions justice. The Hanafi argument is that the saying of a fasiq (sinner) is suspended (mawquf) and thus not authoritative. Additionally, ijma involves honor (takrim), and a sinner does not deserve honor. The text then discusses a counter-argument that honor comes from authority, not vice versa. The author also mentions a view from Shams al-A'imma that a fasiq may be included because he may enter Paradise, but the open sinner (mujin bil fisq) is excluded. The text also discusses the issue of bid'a (innovation). Clear innovations like tajsim (anthropomorphism), rafd (rejection of the Companions), and khuruj (secession) disqualify a mujtahid from being counted in ijma. The majority of Hanafis condition avoidance of bid'a as well as justice. The author argues that innovators are even worse than fasiqs because their opinion is corrupted by desire, while a fasiq's opinion may be sound but his testimony is rejected. The passage ends by noting that the Shafi'is accept narration from an innovator who considers lying forbidden but do not include him in ijma, and the author explains the difference: narration is based on trustworthiness regarding lying, while ijma is based on sound opinion, which innovators lack.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adala): Moral probity; being upright and avoiding major sins.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins.
تكريم (takrim): Honor; ijma confers dignity on its participants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is a fasiq not included in ijma?
A) Because his narration is rejected.
B) Because his opinion is suspended and he does not deserve honor.
C) Because he is not a mujtahid.
D) Because ijma requires all mujtahids, including fasiqs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires 'adala for ijma participants, rejecting the opinion of fasiqs because their word is suspended and they lack the honor ijma confers.

Innovation (Bid'a) as a Disqualifier for Ijma
Stating the condition of avoiding bid'a for mujtahids in ijma and distinguishing between fasiq and mubtadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what constitutes clear innovation (bid'a jaliyya) and explain why innovators are excluded from ijma according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Clear innovation corrupts sound opinion, making the innovator even less reliable than a fasiq for ijma.

The passage extends the condition of 'adala to include avoidance of clear innovation (bid'a jaliyya). Hanafis and the majority require that participants in ijma be free from innovations like anthropomorphism, rejection of the Companions, and secession. The author argues that innovators are even more deserving of exclusion than sinful people because their judgment is corrupted by desire. Let's explore the reasoning and the distinction from the fasiq.

Guided Path
1
Define clear innovation
Identify examples of bid'a jaliyya: tajsim (anthropomorphism), rafd (rejection of the Companions), and khuruj (secession).
These are innovations that affect aqida and practice directly.
2
State the ruling on innovators in ijma
According to the Hanafi school and the majority, innovators (especially those with bid'a jaliyya) are not counted in ijma.
The text says: 'اشتراط عدم البدعة وهي البدعة الجلية كالتجسيم والرفض والخروج كالعدالة'.
3
Compare the innovator with the fasiq
The innovator is worse because his opinion is corrupted by desire (هوى), while the fasiq's opinion may be sound but his word is legally disregarded.
The text: 'أنهم أجدر بعدم الاعتبار من الفاسق فإن الفاسق ما أفسد رأيه، بل أهدر قوله شرعاً'.
4
Address the Shafi'i distinction between narration and ijma
Some Shafi'is accept narration from an innovator who avoids lying but exclude him from ijma. The author explains: narration is about trustworthiness in reporting, while ijma relies on sound opinion, which the innovator lacks.
This shows that different criteria apply to different types of evidence.

بالإعلان في عدم القبول اللهم إلا أن يقال إنه ورد في بعض الأحاديث الوعد بالمغفرة لمن ستر ذنوبه، والوعيد الشديد على من فضحه الله تعالى في الدنيا، وهذا يعطي الظن بالمغفرة لمن ستر ذنوبه وفسقه بخلاف المعلن بوجه بعد إذلالهم وقيل : يعتبر قوله في حق نفسه فقط) فلا يعتبر الإجماع مع مخالفته في حقه ويعتبر في حق غيره (كالإقرار ) فإنه حجة في حقه دون غيره ويدفع بأنه قبل مخالفته كان نافعاً (له) لتكريمه (وإنما يقبل فيما عليه لا فيما له إجماعاً في شرح المختصر، أقول كل ما أدى إليه إجتهاده فيما لا (قاطع) فيه (فهو عليه إجماعاً) يجب عليه العمل به أولاً ولو كان له بالآخرة للتكريم فتدبر، واشتراط عدم البدعة وهي البدعة الجلية كالتجسيم والرفض والخروج ( كالعدالة) فمن شرطها وهم الجمهور والحنفية قاطبة يشترط عدم البدعة أيضاً، ومن لا ،فلا والأول هو الصحيح، كيف لا وأنه قد غلب مكابرة الهوى على العقل وانغمص رأيهم في تعصبهم، فوقعوا في ضلالة وظلمة، فيريهم الهوى خلاف ما هو عليه فلا اعتداد بهم واعتبار القول في الإجماع إنما كان لجامع صحة الرأي فإن قلت ما بال أكثر الشافعية حيث قبلوا رواية المبتدع الذي يرى الكذب حراماً ولا يدخلونهم في الإجماع وما الفرق قلت لعل الفرق عندهم أن مذهبهم أوقعهم فيما أوقعهم ومع ذلك يحرمون الكذب فلا يجترؤون عليه وعدم قبول الرواية كان لريبة الكذب لا غير، وأما الدخول في الإجماع فإنما هو بالرأي، وقد أفسدوه لاختيار مكابرة الهوى على العقل، ونحن قد بينا عدم قبول روايتهم أيضاً، ثم إنه إذا تأملت فيما ألقينا ظهر لك أنهم أجدر بعدم الاعتبار من الفاسق فإن الفاسق ما أفسد رأيه، بل أهدر قوله شرعاً فافهم.
Issue: The justice of the mujtahid is not required in ijma, so it is based on the non-just person according to the chosen view of al-Amidi and Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, may their secrets be sanctified, both from the Shafi'is, because the proofs indicating the authority of ijma are absolute, not restricted to the ummah being just. So considering the ijma of the just and the sinful has no legal basis, and every ruling with no legal basis must be negated. This only holds if the absolute term 'ummah' includes the sinful in ancient custom. The Hanafis, indeed the majority, conditioned justice. And it is the truth, because the saying of a sinful person must be suspended, so he has no role in authority. And because authority in ijma is in reality for honoring its people, and the sinful does not deserve honor. It may be said: No evidence indicates that authority is for honoring; rather, honor is established by authority. Where is this from that? And you are not unaware that we previously indicated in establishing some scriptural proofs that it is for honoring, while it suffices for us that authority entails it. So we say: If their saying were considered in authority, it would necessitate honoring them, which is also negated. It may be said that he is deserving of it, i.e., honor, because of entry into Paradise, for the believer does not remain eternally in Hell. So ijma depends on him. Thus it is transmitted from Imam Shams al-A'imma, except that he excluded the open sinner. And it is not hidden from you that authority does not necessitate restriction by publicity regarding non-acceptance, unless it is said that some hadiths promise forgiveness for one who conceals his sins, and severe threat for one whom Allah exposes in this world. This gives the conjecture of forgiveness for one who conceals his sins and corruption, unlike the open one, who is in doubt. So reflect on it. And it is refuted that he is not considered because of the obligation to suspend judgment on his reports, so he is not deserving of honor by virtue of his saying. So (because it is corrupt?) The third principle: ijma. And this does not contradict honor in the Hereafter at all after their humiliation. And it is said: His saying is considered only in his own right. So ijma is not considered with his opposition regarding him, but it is considered regarding others, like confession. For it is proof regarding him but not others. And it is refuted that before his opposition it was beneficial for him for his honor, and it is accepted in what is against him, not for him by ijma in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. I say: Everything his ijtihad leads to in matters where there is no decisive proof, it is upon him by ijma. He must act on it initially, even if it is for him in the Hereafter for honor, so reflect. And the condition of avoiding innovation, which is clear innovation like anthropomorphism, rejection, and secession, is like justice. So whoever conditions justice, the majority and all Hanafis also condition avoidance of innovation. And whoever does not, does not. The first is correct. How not? For the arrogance of desire has overcome reason, and their opinion has sunk in their fanaticism, so they fall into error and darkness. Desire shows them other than what is true, so they are not considered. And consideration of saying in ijma is only for the collection of sound opinion. If you say: Why do most Shafi'is accept the narration of an innovator who considers lying forbidden but do not include him in ijma? What is the difference? I say: Perhaps the difference with them is that their school has placed them where they have, and yet they forbid lying, so they do not dare to do it. Non-acceptance of narration was only due to suspicion of lying, nothing else. As for inclusion in ijma, it is by opinion, and they have corrupted it by choosing the arrogance of desire over reason. And we have already shown non-acceptance of their narration as well. Then if you reflect on what we have presented, it becomes clear that they are more deserving of non-consideration than the sinful. For the sinful did not corrupt his opinion, but his saying is disregarded legally. So understand.

Key Terms
بدعة جلية (bid'a jaliyya): Clear innovation such as anthropomorphism (tajsim), rejection of Companions (rafd), or secession (khuruj).
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins.
مبتدع (mubtadi'): An innovator, especially one who holds a clear innovation (bid'a jaliyya).

Al-Ijma — Consensus

Defending Historical Ijma: Opposition of Rawafid and Khawarij
Defending ijma against anachronistic and illegitimate opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for valid ijma by distinguishing between anachronistic opposition and contemporaneous dissent from unqualified mujtahids.

Core Idea
Post-ijma dissent does not break consensus; only contemporaneous valid mujtahid opposition matters.

This lesson examines a critical usul al-fiqh objection: does the existence of dissenting groups like the Rawafid and Khawarij invalidate the historical ijma on the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Ali? The Hanafi response provides a nuanced condition for when opposition affects ijma, arguing that anachronistic dissent or opposition from those not qualified as mujtahids cannot undermine a validly concluded consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Recognize the challenge: if ijma requires absence of clear innovation, then the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Ali would lack ijma due to Rawafid (reject Abu Bakr) and Khawarij (opposed Ali).
The objection targets scholars who do not condition avoidance of bid'a (clear innovation) in the consensus group.
2
Analyze the first answer: Rawafid
The Rawafid emerged after the Companions' ijma on Abu Bakr. Their later denial of the ijma is irrelevant because it postdates the consensus.
The text says: 'Ijma was concluded in the time of the Companions, and they (Rawafid) came later.'
3
Analyze the second answer: Khawarij
Mu'awiya, the leader of the opposition to Ali, did not pledge allegiance, so there was no complete ijma. However, the caliphate of Ali was established by the majority of reliable people and his merit, not by full consensus. The text argues Mu'awiya was not a valid mujtahid, so his opposition does not invalidate the overall legitimacy.
The text questions Mu'awiya's status as a mujtahid, citing that he did not engage in proper debate and was considered an unjust ruler by al-Hidayah.
4
Examine the critique of Mu'awiya's ijtihad
The passage presents evidence that Mu'awiya's opposition was not based on valid ijtihad: he avoided debate, made weak arguments (e.g., about 'Ammar), and is not recorded to have issued fatwas on usul al-fiqh. Therefore, his dissent does not break ijma.
Additional point: Usama ibn Zayd, a prominent Companion, also doubted Ali's matter, indicating no full consensus, but the majority still suffices.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that ijma on both caliphates is valid. The opposition of anachronistic groups (Rawafid) or unqualified individuals (Mu'awiya as non-mujtahid) does not undermine a consensus formed by the qualified majority.
The practical implication: many historical ijma are protected from being invalidated by later or illegitimate dissent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما كان يرد على غير شارطي انتفاء البدعة الجلية أنه يلزم أن لا ينعقد الاجماع على خلافة أفضل الصديقين وأمير المؤمنين على الخلاف الروافض في الأول والخوارج في الثاني، أجاب عن الأول بقوله (وخلاف الروافض بعد الاجماع) فإن الإجماع انعقد زمن الصحابة، وهم حدثوا بعدهم بكثير، وإنكارهم حدوثهم، ودعوى أنه كان مذهبهم من قبل كذب ومكابرة لا يلتفت إليه، وأجاب عن الثاني بقوله وخلاف الخوارج ليس في الاجماع لأن معاوية مجتهد) وهو لم يبايع أمير المؤمنين علياً كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام فما انعقد الاجماع، وأما ثبوت الخلافة فلكفاية بيعة الأكثر من المعتبرين وكونه اهلاً لها في نفسه من غير ارتياب أو لدليل آخر لاح لهم (فتأمل) وقال بعضهم في كون مخالفة معاوية بالاجتهاد نظر، لأنه لو كانت بالاجتهاد لناظر بالحجة وأمير المؤمنين على كان ألين للحق وقصد مناظرته بالحجة، وإقامة الحجة عليه، ولم يصغ إليه وعند شهادة عمار ، قال : إنما قتله علي حيث جاء به كبيراً، وليس من الحجة في شيء، ولذا قال أمير المؤمنين في الجواب : فإذا قتل حمزة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، بل الكلام في كونه مجتهداً ، كيف وقد عده صاحب «الهداية» من السلاطين الجائرة مقابل العادلين ولو كان بالاجتهاد لما كان جوراً، ولم ينقل عنه فتوى على طريقة الأصول الشرعية هذا والأولى أن يقال : لم يكن إجماعاً لما كان أسامة حب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم شاكاً في أمير المؤمنين، فإنه أرسل مولاه إليه، وقال في اعتذار عدم دخوله في أمره لو كنت في شدق الأسد أحببت أن أكون معك فيه، ولكن هذا الأمر لم أره رواه البخاري وعن أبي وائل قال: دخل أبو موسى وأبو مسعود على
Then, since it was objected to those who do not condition avoidance of clear innovation that it would necessitate that ijma would not have been concluded on the caliphate of the best of the two Siddiqs (Abu Bakr) and the Commander of the Faithful (Ali) due to the opposition of the Rawafid in the first and the Khawarij in the second. He answered the first by his saying: 'And the opposition of the Rawafid is after ijma.' For ijma was concluded in the time of the Companions, and they (Rawafid) came later. Their denial of that and their claim that it was their school from before is a lie and arrogance not to be heeded. He answered the second by his saying: 'And the opposition of the Khawarij is not in the ijma because Mu'awiya was a mujtahid.' He did not pledge allegiance to the Commander of the Faithful Ali, so ijma was not concluded. As for the establishment of the caliphate, it sufficed the pledge of the majority of reliable people and his being qualified for it in himself without doubt, or due to another evidence that became clear to them. So reflect. Some said regarding the opposition of Mu'awiya being ijtihad: there is consideration. For if it were ijtihad, he would have debated with evidence. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali was more gentle towards the truth and intended to debate him with evidence and establish evidence upon him, but he did not listen to him. And at the testimony of 'Ammar, he said: 'Ali killed him because he brought him as an elder,' which is not evidence at all. Therefore the Commander of the Faithful said in response: 'If so, then Hamza was killed by the Messenger of Allah?' Rather, the discussion is about his being a mujtahid. How can he be considered so when the author of al-Hidayah considered him among the unjust rulers as opposed to the just? And if it were by ijtihad, it would not be injustice. And no fatwa from him is transmitted according to the method of legal principles. The better view is to say: It was not ijma because Usama, the beloved of the Messenger of Allah, was doubtful about the Commander of the Faithful. He sent his servant to him and said in apology for not entering into his matter: 'If I were in the lion's jaw, I would love to be with you, but this matter I do not see (as correct).' [Bukhari narrated it] And from Abu Wa'il: Abu Musa and Abu Mas'ud entered upon...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage addresses a common objection against the condition of avoiding clear innovation in ijma. The objection is that if innovators are excluded, then ijma could not have been concluded on the caliphate of Abu Bakr because the Rawafid (Shi'a who reject his caliphate) opposed it, and on the caliphate of Ali because the Khawarij (who seceded from him) opposed it. The author provides two answers. First, regarding the Rawafid: their opposition came after the ijma of the Companions had already been concluded. They are later innovators, and their claim that they always held that belief is false. Second, regarding the Khawarij: their opposition is not against ijma because Mu'awiya (the leader of the opposition to Ali) was a mujtahid who did not pledge allegiance, so there was no complete consensus. The caliphate of Ali was established by the majority pledge of reliable people and his qualifications. The author then critiques the claim that Mu'awiya's opposition was valid ijtihad, citing that Mu'awiya was not a true mujtahid but considered an unjust ruler. The text also mentions that Usama, a prominent Companion, was doubtful about Ali's matter, indicating that there was not full consensus. The passage ends abruptly with a narration from Abu Wa'il about Abu Musa and Abu Mas'ud, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
روافض (Rawafid): A group of Shia who reject the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar.
خوارج (Khawarij): A group that seceded from Ali's camp and opposed his caliphate.
مجتهد (mujtahid): One qualified to perform ijtihad; in this context, the text questions whether Mu'awiyah was a mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author claim that the opposition of the Rawafid does not invalidate the ijma on Abu Bakr's caliphate?
A) Because Rawafid are not Muslims.
B) Because their opposition occurred after the ijma of the Companions had already taken place.
C) Because Abu Bakr was not the rightful caliph.
D) Because Rawafid are not considered people of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Anachronistic opposition or dissent from unqualified individuals does not break a validly concluded ijma; only contemporaneous dissent from qualified mujtahids matters.

Conditions for Ijma: 'Adalah and Absence of Grave Bid'ah
Conditions for inclusion in Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition of 'adalah and absence of grave bid'ah to determine whether an individual's opinion counts in ijma, and evaluate the distinction between narration and opinion in the context of ijma disputes.

Core Idea
Grave innovation corrupts the opinion so severely that it is disregarded in ijma—even more than a fasiq's.

This passage discusses a key condition for the validity of ijma: the uprightness ('adalah) of the scholars involved and the absence of grave innovation (bid'ah jaliyyah). The Hanafi school, along with the majority, requires both. The author explains why grave innovators are excluded: their relentless desire (hawa) has corrupted their reasoning, making their opinion unreliable. He also clarifies the difference between accepting narrations from innovators (which some Shafi'is do) and including them in ijma (which no one does).

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that absence of grave bid'ah is required just like 'adalah. What is the precise condition?
Grave bid'ah includes tajsim, rafd, and khuruj.
2
Understand the rationale
The author argues that grave innovation causes desire to overcome reason, corrupting the opinion. How does this affect the reliability of the individual's view?
The opinion is considered unsound, so it cannot contribute to ijma.
3
Examine the Shafi'i distinction
Some Shafi'is accept narrations from innovators but exclude them from ijma. What is the basis for this distinction?
Narration depends on veracity; opinion depends on soundness of reasoning.
4
Compare with a fasiq
The author states that a grave innovator is even less worthy of consideration than a fasiq. Why is that?
A fasiq has not corrupted his opinion, only his actions; an innovator has corrupted his reasoning.
5
Apply the rule
In a given case, determine if a scholar is a grave innovator; if so, his opinion does not prevent ijma.
If he is not a grave innovator, his opinion must be considered unless he is a fasiq (disregarded legally).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثالث الإجماع وهذا لا ينافي التكريم في الآخرة بوجه بعد إذلالهم وقيل : يعتبر قوله في حق نفسه فقط) فلا يعتبر الإجماع مع مخالفته في حقه ويعتبر في حق غيره (كالإقرار ) فإنه حجة في حقه دون غيره ويدفع بأنه قبل مخالفته كان نافعاً (له) لتكريمه (وإنما يقبل فيما عليه لا فيما له إجماعاً في شرح المختصر، أقول كل ما أدى إليه إجتهاده فيما لا (قاطع) فيه (فهو عليه إجماعاً) يجب عليه العمل به أولاً ولو كان له بالآخرة للتكريم فتدبر، واشتراط عدم البدعة وهي البدعة الجلية كالتجسيم والرفض والخروج ( كالعدالة) فمن شرطها وهم الجمهور والحنفية قاطبة يشترط عدم البدعة أيضاً، ومن لا ،فلا والأول هو الصحيح، كيف لا وأنه قد غلب مكابرة الهوى على العقل وانغمص رأيهم في تعصبهم، فوقعوا في ضلالة وظلمة، فيريهم الهوى خلاف ما هو عليه فلا اعتداد بهم واعتبار القول في الإجماع إنما كان لجامع صحة الرأي فإن قلت ما بال أكثر الشافعية حيث قبلوا رواية المبتدع الذي يرى الكذب حراماً ولا يدخلونهم في الإجماع وما الفرق قلت لعل الفرق عندهم أن مذهبهم أوقعهم فيما أوقعهم ومع ذلك يحرمون الكذب فلا يجترؤون عليه وعدم قبول الرواية كان لريبة الكذب لا غير، وأما الدخول في الإجماع فإنما هو بالرأي، وقد أفسدوه لاختيار مكابرة الهوى على العقل، ونحن قد بينا عدم قبول روايتهم أيضاً، ثم إنه إذا تأملت فيما ألقينا ظهر لك أنهم أجدر بعدم الاعتبار من الفاسق فإن الفاسق ما أفسد رأيه، بل أهدر قوله شرعاً فافهم.
The third source is Ijma, and this does not contradict honor in the afterlife in any way after their humiliation. And it was said: his statement is considered only in his own right, so ijma is not considered with his opposition in his own right, but it is considered regarding others, like an acknowledgment; it is proof in his own right but not regarding others. It is rebutted that before his opposition it was beneficial to him for his honor, and it is accepted only against him, not for him, by consensus in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. I say: everything that his ijtihad leads to in matters without a decisive text is binding upon him by consensus; he must act upon it first, even if he may have honor in the afterlife; reflect. And the condition of the absence of innovation – which is grave innovation such as anthropomorphism, Rafd, and Khuruj – is like uprightness. Those who stipulate uprightness, namely the majority and the Hanafis collectively, also stipulate absence of innovation. Those who do not stipulate uprightness do not stipulate it, and the first is correct. How could it not be? For the obstinacy of desire has overcome reason, and their opinion has become weak in their fanaticism, so they fell into error and darkness; desire shows them the opposite of what is true, so they are not to be regarded. Consideration of a statement in ijma is only due to the soundness of opinion. If you ask: why do most Shafi'is accept the narration of an innovator who considers lying forbidden, yet they do not include him in ijma? What is the difference? I say: perhaps the difference according to them is that their doctrine led them to what it led, yet they still forbid lying so they do not dare to commit it, and the non-acceptance of narration is only due to suspicion of lying, nothing else. As for inclusion in ijma, it is by opinion, and they have corrupted it by choosing obstinacy of desire over reason. And we have already shown that we also do not accept their narration. Then, if you reflect on what we have presented, it becomes clear that they deserve non-consideration more than a sinful person, for the sinful person has not corrupted his opinion; rather, his statement is disregarded legally. Understand.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition of 'adalah (uprightness) and avoidance of bid'ah (innovation) for those whose consensus is considered binding. The author states that the Hanafis and the majority require both 'adalah and absence of grave innovation (bid'ah jaliyyah, such as anthropomorphism, Rafd, or Kharijite rebellion). The reasoning is that such innovations corrupt the faculty of opinion by allowing desire to overcome reason, rendering the individual's view unreliable. The author then answers a potential objection: the Shafi'is accept narrations from innovators (who still consider lying forbidden) but exclude them from ijma. The distinction is that narration depends on veracity, while ijma depends on sound opinion; innovators have corrupted their opinion through obstinacy, thus their consensus is worthless, even more so than a fasiq (sinner) who has not corrupted his opinion but merely acts against it. The author concludes by emphasizing that such people are even less worthy of consideration than a fasiq.

Key Terms
البدعة الجلية (al-bid'ah al-jaliyyah): Grave innovation such as anthropomorphism (tajsim), Rafd (rejection of the first two caliphs), or Khuruj (rebellion against legitimate rulers).
العدالة (al-'adalah): Uprightness, including avoidance of major sins and innovation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the opinion of a grave innovator not considered in ijma?
A) Because he is a sinner and sinners are not reliable.
B) Because his opinion is corrupted by desire overcoming reason.
C) Because he is not a mujtahid.
D) Because he opposes the consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
Grave innovation disqualifies a scholar from being counted in ijma because it corrupts the soundness of opinion, making it unreliable.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

Defending Ijma: The Objections of Rawafid and Khawarij
Refuting objections that Rawafid and Khawarij invalidate ijma on caliphate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that later opposition does not break a valid ijma, and evaluate the claim that opposition based on ijtihad prevents ijma from forming.

Core Idea
Later opposition does not break a valid ijma; but legitimate ijtihad can prevent its formation.

This passage addresses a key challenge to the Hanafi position on ijma: if some later groups (Rawafid and Khawarij) opposed the caliphates of Abu Bakr and 'Ali, does that invalidate the historical ijma? The author presents a nuanced defense, distinguishing between opposition that arises after ijma has been formed and opposition that prevents ijma from ever being reached. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi theory of ijma and its role in establishing political legitimacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
The first objection is from the Rawafid who reject Abu Bakr's caliphate. The second is from the Khawarij who opposed 'Ali. Notice that the author treats them differently based on timing.
Rawafid = emerged after ijma on Abu Bakr; Khawarij = contemporary opposition from Mu'awiya based on ijtihad.
2
Apply the Hanafi response to the first objection
The author states that the Rawafid appeared after the ijma of the Companions on Abu Bakr. Since ijma once formed is binding, later disagreement does not break it. This is a core Hanafi principle.
The burden is on the Rawafid to prove they held that view from the beginning, which the author dismisses as false.
3
Analyse the second objection and the counter-argument
For 'Ali, the objection is that the Khawarij (especially Mu'awiya) opposed him, so no ijma existed. The author first suggests Mu'awiya was a mujtahid, thus his opposition is legitimate and prevents ijma. However, a counter-argument is presented: Mu'awiya's actions were not ijtihad but oppression, based on evidence from al-Hidayah and his refusal to debate.
The author ultimately favours a different explanation: even respected Companions doubted 'Ali's cause, so there was no ijma anyway.
4
Evaluate the evidence from hadith
The author cites Bukhari narrations that Usama, Abu Musa, Abu Mas'ud, and Abu Bakra were doubtful about 'Ali's affair. This shows that ijma on 'Ali was not achieved among the Companions themselves.
These narrations are used as dalil naqli to demonstrate the absence of ijma, not as proof of a ruling.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi position is that ijma on Abu Bakr stands; ijma on 'Ali was never formed due to legitimate differences. Both caliphates remain valid by majority pledge and personal worthiness.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the caliphate is valid despite later or contemporary opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما كان يرد على غير شارطي انتفاء البدعة الجلية أنه يلزم أن لا ينعقد الاجماع على خلافة أفضل الصديقين وأمير المؤمنين على الخلاف الروافض في الأول والخوارج في الثاني، أجاب عن الأول بقوله (وخلاف الروافض بعد الاجماع) فإن الإجماع انعقد زمن الصحابة، وهم حدثوا بعدهم بكثير، وإنكارهم حدوثهم، ودعوى أنه كان مذهبهم من قبل كذب ومكابرة لا يلتفت إليه، وأجاب عن الثاني بقوله وخلاف الخوارج ليس في الاجماع لأن معاوية مجتهد) وهو لم يبايع أمير المؤمنين علياً كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام فما انعقد الاجماع، وأما ثبوت الخلافة فلكفاية بيعة الأكثر من المعتبرين وكونه اهلاً لها في نفسه من غير ارتياب أو لدليل آخر لاح لهم (فتأمل) وقال بعضهم في كون مخالفة معاوية بالاجتهاد نظر، لأنه لو كانت بالاجتهاد لناظر بالحجة وأمير المؤمنين على كان ألين للحق وقصد مناظرته بالحجة، وإقامة الحجة عليه، ولم يصغ إليه وعند شهادة عمار ، قال : إنما قتله علي حيث جاء به كبيراً، وليس من الحجة في شيء، ولذا قال أمير المؤمنين في الجواب : فإذا قتل حمزة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، بل الكلام في كونه مجتهداً ، كيف وقد عده صاحب «الهداية» من السلاطين الجائرة مقابل العادلين ولو كان بالاجتهاد لما كان جوراً، ولم ينقل عنه فتوى على طريقة الأصول الشرعية هذا والأولى أن يقال : لم يكن إجماعاً لما كان أسامة حب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم شاكاً في أمير المؤمنين، فإنه أرسل مولاه إليه، وقال في اعتذار عدم دخوله في أمره لو كنت في شدق الأسد أحببت أن أكون معك فيه، ولكن هذا الأمر لم أره رواه البخاري وعن أبي وائل قال: دخل أبو موسى وأبو مسعود على عمار حين بعثه عليّ إلى أهل الكوفة يستفزهم فقالا: ما رأيناك أتيت أمراً أكره عندنا من اسراعك في هذا الأمر منذ أسلمت! فقال عمار لهما مثله رواه البخاري، وأبو بكرة أيضاً عد هذا القتال من الفتنة وإذا كان أمثال أسامة وأبي مسعود وأبي موسى وأبو بكرة شاكين في أمره فأين الإجماع؟ وبعد التنزل فالجواب بحدوثهم بعد الإجماع فافهم.
Then, because it might be objected to those who do not stipulate the absence of grave innovation that it would follow that no consensus could be formed on the caliphate of the best of the two truthful ones (Abu Bakr) and the Commander of the Faithful ('Ali) due to the opposition of the Rafidites concerning the former and the Kharijites concerning the latter. He answered the first by saying: 'The opposition of the Rafidites came after the consensus.' For consensus was formed during the time of the Companions, and they originated much later. Their denial of this and their claim that it was their doctrine from before is false and obstinate, not to be heeded. He answered the second by saying: 'The opposition of the Kharijites is not (a break in) consensus, because Mu'awiya was a mujtahid.' He did not pledge allegiance to the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali, may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family, so no consensus was formed. As for the establishment of the caliphate, it was sufficient due to the pledge of the majority of those who count, and his worthiness for it in himself without doubt, or due to another indication that occurred to them. (Ponder). And some said: there is a problem with considering Mu'awiya's opposition as ijtihad, because if it were ijtihad, he would have debated with evidence, and 'Ali was more yielding to truth and intended to debate with evidence and establish proof against him, but he did not listen. And at the testimony of 'Ammar, he said: 'Verily, he was killed by 'Ali where he brought him old,' and that is not proof at all. Hence the Commander of the Faithful said in reply: 'Then Hamza was killed by the Messenger of Allah...' Rather, the discussion is about whether he was a mujtahid. How so, when the author of al-Hidayah considered him among the oppressive rulers as opposed to the just ones? If he were a mujtahid, it would not be oppression. And no legal verdict (fatwa) is transmitted from him according to the method of the principles of Sharia. And the better is to say: there was no consensus because Usama, the beloved of the Messenger of Allah, was doubtful about the Commander of the Faithful. He sent his freed slave to him and said in apology for not entering his affair: 'If I were in the lion's mouth, I would love to be with you, but this matter I did not see it.' Bukhari narrated it. And from Abu Wa'il: Abu Musa and Abu Mas'ud entered upon 'Ammar when 'Ali sent him to the people of Kufa to mobilize them, and they said: 'We have not seen you do anything more detestable to us than your haste in this matter since you embraced Islam!' So 'Ammar said the like to them. Bukhari narrated it. And Abu Bakra also considered this fighting as fitna. If such people as Usama, Abu Mas'ud, Abu Musa, and Abu Bakra were doubtful about his affair, where is the consensus? Even after conceding, the answer is that they originated after the consensus. Understand.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage defends the validity of ijma on the caliphates of Abu Bakr and 'Ali despite the objections of the Rawafid (who reject Abu Bakr) and the Khawarij (who opposed 'Ali). The author presents the standard Hanafi defense: the Rafidites emerged after the consensus of the Companions on Abu Bakr's caliphate, so their later opposition does not break the earlier ijma. As for the Kharijites, the objection is that Mu'awiya's opposition meant no ijma formed. The author argues that Mu'awiya was a mujtahid, and since he did not pledge allegiance, there was no ijma in the first place; the caliphate was established by the majority pledge and 'Ali's inherent worthiness. However, the author then reports a counter-argument that Mu'awiya's opposition was not legitimate ijtihad, citing that he refused debate, was called oppressive by al-Hidayah, and no fatwa from him is recorded. The better explanation, according to the author, is that there simply was no ijma because even respected Companions like Usama, Abu Musa, Abu Mas'ud, and Abu Bakra were doubtful about 'Ali's cause, as shown in hadith. Nevertheless, the author finally falls back on the 'delay' argument: these doubters also postdated the initial ijma. The overall conclusion is that ijma on the caliphate is not invalidated by later opposition.

Key Terms
الروافض (al-rawafid): A sect that rejects the first two caliphs and holds that 'Ali was the rightful immediate successor.
الخوارج (al-khawarij): A sect that rebels against the ruler and holds that 'Ali was in error in the arbitration.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of mujtahids of the Muslim community on a legal ruling after the Prophet's death.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning by a qualified scholar to derive rulings from the sources.
البيعة (al-bay'ah): Pledge of allegiance to a caliph or leader.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author answer the objection that the Rawafid's opposition breaks the ijma on Abu Bakr's caliphate?
A) By saying the Rawafid were not qualified to be part of ijma.
B) By saying the Rawafid emerged after the ijma had already been formed among the Companions.
C) By saying the Rawafid are liars.
D) By saying there was no ijma on Abu Bakr.

Key Takeaway
Later opposition does not break a valid ijma; legitimate ijtihad can prevent its formation, but the Hanafi school upholds the caliphates of Abu Bakr and 'Ali through majority acceptance and personal worthiness.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

The Binding Nature of Ijma Across Generations
Defending the authoritativeness of post-Sahaba ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the scriptural and rational arguments to defend the binding nature of ijma of later generations and rebut the Zahiri objection.

Core Idea
Ijma of every era is binding; the Quranic 'way of the believers' and the universal practice of charging error prove it.

A critical debate in usul al-fiqh is whether the consensus of scholars after the Companions carries the same legal authority. Some, like the Zahiris, restrict binding ijma to the Companions only. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi (majority) argument that ijma is binding for every generation, using both scriptural proofs and a rational observation of how scholars treat disagreement with consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine whether ijma of non-Sahabah is a hujjah (binding proof) or not.
The Zahiris and one opinion of Ahmad hold it is not; the majority (including Hanafis) hold it is.
2
Analyze the scriptural proof (dalil sam'i)
The Quranic phrases 'way of the believers' (سبيل المؤمنين) and 'the community' (الأمة) are general, applying to believers of all times. This indicates that following the consensus of any era is obligatory.
No specific verse is quoted, but the author alludes to Q4:115.
3
Examine the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
Scholars in every age considered opposing an established ijma as an error (takhTi'a). This shows that the authoritativeness of ijma is ingrained in the Muslim mind; if ijma were not binding, the charge of error would not be justified.
The proof works inductively: by surveying cases, we see that ijma is treated as a definitive proof.
4
Consider the Zahiri objection and its rebuttal
The Zahiris argue that the Companions agreed that ijtihad is permissible in non-qat'i matters, so a later ijma would close ijtihad and lead to contradiction. The Hanafi response: the Companions themselves made ijma on some rulings, which also closes ijtihad; thus, the Zahiri objection is self-refuting.
The author says 'this is refuted by the Companions' own ijma on a ruling.'
5
Synthesize the outcome
The correct view (صحيح) is that ijma of later generations is binding. This has practical implications: rulings established by post-Sahabi ijma are definitive and cannot be reopened.
The author explicitly states 'وهو الصحيح' — and this is the correct view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الإجماع الحجة لا يختص بالصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، بل اجماع من بعدهم أيضاً حجة خلافاً للظاهرية وعليه الشيخ الأكبر خاتم الولاية المحمدية وابن حبان (ولأحمد) الإمام (قولان) قول كالظاهرية، وقول كالجمهور، وهو الصحيح لنا: الأدلة السمعية، فإنها ليست مختصة بالحاضرين على المختار فإن سبيل المؤمنين والأمة يتناول كل عصر (وأما) الأدلة العقلية فقيل : تتم في غيرهم أيضاً (وقيل : (لا) تتم (لأنهم) أي الأخيار من الأمة (خصوا التخطئة بمخالفة إجماع الصحابة لا بمخالفة كل إجماع (أقول الحق الاتفاق على التخطئة) بمخالفة الإجماع (مطلقاً كما قيل كما يظهر باستقراء الوقائع (لكن لا ينتهض ههنا) حجة (لأن الخصم ينكر إمكان وقوعه وهو لا ينافي التخطئة على تقدير وقوعه فافهم فإنه دقيق فيه إشارة إلى الفرق بين انتهاض السمعية وعدم انتهاض العقلية، أن الظاهر أنهما مع سواء، ووجه الفرق أن مقتضى السمعية أن الحجية لازمة لوقوع الاتفاق مطلقاً، ومقتضى العقلية ليس كذلك، بل مقتضاها أنه إذا وجد الاتفاق وصار حجة صح تخطئة مخالفه، فلو وقع الاتفاق ولا عبرة به كما قال الخصم لا ينافي ذلك نعم : ينافي السمعية لأنه اتفاق على ما ليس بحق كذا في الحاشية». وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن صحة تخطئة المخالف غير متوقفة على الحجية في العلم، ولو توقفت في الخارج، وحاصل الاستدلال أنهم يخطئون مخالف ما وقع عليه الاتفاق في كل عصر فلو لم يكن اتفاقهم حجة وصواباً عندهم لما ثبت التخطئة فكون الإجماع حجة قطعية مركوز في أذهانهم، ولا يكون هذا إلا عن قاطع، وهذا بعينه جار في إجماع التابعين ومن بعدهم، فالتخطئة لو وجدت تنافي عدم الحجية قطعاً، وإن أراد أن التخطئة في نفس الأمر متوقفة على الحجية فهذا غير ضار بل نافع، ثم إنه لو كان تخطئة المخالف غير مناف لعدم العبرة بالاتفاق بعد تحققه لم يتم هذا الدليل أصلاً، فإن للخصم أن يقول : هذا إنما يتم لو كان إجماع الصحابة حجة معتبرة، وأما لو كان غير معتبر كما يقول به الخصم فالتخطئة هذا لا تنافي ذلك هذا فإذن لم يبق فارق بعد تسليم التخطئة بين العقلية والسمعية ولم يبق في كلام إلا بأن الخصم ينكر تحقق الاتفاق فالتخطئة على تقدير تحققه لا تنافي ذلك ومثل هذا تحققها في السمعية أيضاً، فالجواب حينئذ بإثبات وقوع اتفاق التابعين في حادثة ولم يثبت إنكار الخصم إلا عند استقرار الخلاف وتقرر المذاهب لا عند سكوت الصحابة لعدم وقوع هذه الحادثة في زمنهم، ومحل الخلاف ههنا هو هذا إلا ذاك، فإنه مسألة أخرى بيانها إن شاء الله، الظاهرية قالوا : أولاً أجمع الصحابة على أن ما لا قاطع فيه محل الاجتهاد) ولا بأس برجوعه إلى أي طرف شاء (فلو قيل بإجماع من بعدهم لأبطله إذ لا يبقى حينئذ محل الاجتهاد ولزم النقيضان) لحقية كل اجماع (قلنا) هذا (منقوض بإجماع الصحابة) على حكم (بعد هذا ، سيجيء
Issue: IJma' as proof is not specific to the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them; rather, the consensus of those after them is also proof, contrary to the Zahiris. And this is the view of the Greatest Shaykh, the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood, and Ibn Hibban. (And from Imam Ahmad) there are two opinions: one like the Zahiris, and one like the majority, which is correct. For us: the scriptural proofs (adillah sam'iyyah) are not specific to those present, according to the chosen view, for 'the way of the believers' and 'the community' encompasses every era. (As for) rational proofs, it is said they are also complete in others. (And it is said: they are not complete because they (the elite of the community) specify the charge of error (takhTia) to opposing the ijma of the Companions, not to opposing every ijma. I say: the truth is that the charge of error is agreed upon for opposing ijma absolutely, as is said, as appears from induction of cases. But it does not stand as a proof here because the opponent denies its occurrence, and it does not contradict the charge of error assuming it occurs. Understand, for it is subtle. It indicates the difference between the force of scriptural proofs and the non-force of rational proofs. Apparently, they are equal. The point of difference is that the requirement of scriptural proofs is that authoritativeness is necessarily attached to the occurrence of agreement absolutely, whereas the requirement of rational proofs is not so; rather, its requirement is that when agreement occurs and becomes proof, the charge of error against its opponent is valid. So if agreement occurs and it is disregarded as the opponent says, that does not contradict that. But it does contradict the scriptural proof because it would be an agreement on something not true, as in the gloss. And you should not be unaware that the validity of charging the opponent with error is not dependent on the authoritativeness in knowledge, even if it were dependent externally. The gist of the argument is that they charge with error those who oppose what they have agreed upon in every era. If their agreement were not proof and correct in their view, the charge of error would not be established. The fact that ijma is a definitive proof is ingrained in their minds, and this only comes from a definitive source. This same reasoning applies to the ijma of the Successors and those after them. Therefore, if the charge of error exists, it definitely contradicts non-authoritativeness. If he means that the charge of error in reality depends on authoritativeness, this is not harmful but beneficial. Then, if charging the opponent with error is not incompatible with disregarding the agreement after it occurs, this proof would not stand at all. For the opponent can say: This holds only if the ijma of the Companions is considered proof; but if it is not considered proof as the opponent holds, then the charge of error does not contradict that. So there remains no difference after conceding the charge of error between rational and scriptural proofs. Nothing remains in the statement except that the opponent denies the occurrence of agreement; then the charge of error assuming its occurrence does not contradict that. The same applies to scriptural proofs. The answer then is to establish the occurrence of the Successors' agreement on an incident. The opponent has not denied it except after the establishment of disagreement and the determination of schools, not at the time of silence of the Companions due to the incident not occurring in their time. The locus of disagreement here is exactly that, though it is another issue. Its explanation will come, God willing. The Zahiris said: First, the Companions agreed that matters without a decisive text are subject to ijtihad, and there is no problem in him choosing any side. So if one says there is ijma of those after them, it would annul that, because then there would remain no room for ijtihad, and two contradictories would follow for every true ijma. We say: This is refuted by the Companions' own consensus on a ruling. After this, it will come.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on whether ijma is binding only from the Companions or from all generations. The author sides with the majority (including the senior Sufi saint, Ibn Hibban, and the preferred view of Ahmad ibn Hanbal) that ijma of later generations is also proof, contrary to the Zahiris. The scriptural proofs (such as 'the way of the believers' and 'the community' in the Quran) are general for all times. Rational proofs are also put forward: the fact that scholars charge opponents of ijma with error in every era shows that ijma is considered authoritative. The author analyzes a subtle point: if the opponent denies that later ijma can occur, then the charge of error on its occurrence does not contradict that denial; but scriptural proofs would still affirm it. The argument from charging with error is that it is ingrained in Muslim minds that ijma is definitive proof, and this applies to all eras. However, the opponent may say that the charge of error only relates to the Companions' ijma. The author responds by insisting that the same reasoning applies to later ijma. The Zahiri objection is that the Companions themselves agreed that ijtihad is permissible in non-textual matters, so a later ijma would close ijtihad and thus be contradictory. The author replies by noting that the Companions also made ijma on certain rulings, which could similarly close ijtihad; so the Zahiri argument is self-refuting. The discussion ends with a promise to further explain.

Key Terms
التخطئة (al-takhTi'a): The act of declaring an opponent's view to be wrong because it opposes ijma.
السمعية (al-sam'iyyah): Scriptural proofs; evidences derived from the Quran and Sunnah.
العقلية (al-'aqliyyah): Rational proofs; evidences derived from reason and observation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the flaw in the Zahiri argument that a later ijma would close the door of ijtihad?
A) Ijtihad is always permissible even after ijma.
B) The Companions themselves made ijma on rulings, which also closes ijtihad.
C) Later ijma does not prevent ijtihad.
D) The Zahiris misinterpret the word 'ijma'.

Key Takeaway
Ijma of later generations is binding; both scriptural proofs (Quranic generality) and rational proofs (universal charge of error) establish its authoritativeness, and the Zahiri objection fails because the Companions themselves practiced binding ijma.

The Minimum Number for Ijma: Tawatur Not Required
Parsing the minimum number requirement for ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ijma does not require a specific number of scholars and identify the Hanafi position on the minimum number for ijma according to the chosen view.

Core Idea
Ijma is authoritative as an honor for the ummah, not because of any specific number of scholars.

This passage tackles a foundational question in usul al-fiqh: how many scholars are needed for ijma (consensus) to be a binding proof? The author clarifies that ijma does not depend on the large number associated with tawatur. Instead, its authority is devotional (ta‘abbudī) from scriptural proofs. The passage then presents different scholarly views on the minimum number, culminating in the chosen Hanafi view that even a single mujtahid can be the locus of ijma if he is the only one present, ensuring that truth never leaves the ummah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim of the passage
State the main thesis: ijma does not require the number of tawatur. Explain what 'tawatur number' means and why it is irrelevant for ijma.
Tawatur is a condition for certainty in sensory matters, but ijma's authority is based on honor (karāma) and scriptural proof, not on raw numbers.
2
Distinguish the three opinions on the minimum number
List the three positions: (1) a group (jamā‘a) is required, agreement of two is not ijma; (2) two suffice if they are the only mujtahids; (3) a single mujtahid suffices and his opinion is proof.
Each opinion is supported by a different interpretation of the hadith 'My community will not agree on error' and the hadith blaming opposition to the group.
3
Pinpoint the Hanafi chosen view (al-mukhtār)
State that the chosen view (mufta bihi) is that the opinion of a single mujtahid (when he is the only one) is hujja. Explain the reasoning: negating error from the community includes the individual; otherwise, there would be no one to enjoin good.
This view is based on the idea that truth must remain accessible within the ummah, and the hadith 'my community will not agree on error' implies the infallibility of the collective, which extends to the solitary mujtahid when he is the sole representative.
4
Analyze the authority basis (ta‘abbudī vs rational)
The passage asserts that the authority (hujjiyya) of ijma is established through scriptural proofs (adilla sam‘iyya), not rational ones. Rational proofs cannot demonstrate that a non-tawatur number of scholars is infallible.
This highlights the devotional nature of ijma: it is honored as a proof because of the hadith, not because of any inherent rational necessity.
