⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: لا يشترط عدد التواتر في المجمعين (في مختار الأكثر) ليس المراد بعدد التواتر العدد المعين فإنه قد تقدم أنه لا حد لأقله، بل المراد عدد لو أخبروا في محسوس وقع العلم لأن الحجية) إنما هي للاتفاق تكريماً لهذه الأمة وهو مطلق لا دخل فيه لعدد التواتر، أعلم أن العمدة في إثبات حجية هذا الإجماع الدلائل السمعية، أما العقلية فلا تفيد لأن التخطئة لم تظهر لمخالف المجمعين الغير البالغين عدد التواتر كما لا يخفى ولذا قال المصنف الحجية للإجماع تعبدي تكريماً فافهم (فجمع) قالوا لا بد من جماعة ولا يكون اتفاق الاثنين ولو كانا كل الأمة المجتهدة إجماعاً لوقوع ذم مخالفة الجماعة في الحديث (وقيل يكفي اثنان) إذا كانا كل الأمة المجتهدين وهو الظاهر، وإلا لزم إجماع الأمة على الخطأ (أما الواحد) إذا كان هو المجتهد لا غير فقيل حجة لئلا يخرج الحق عن (الأمة وتحقيق مناط لا تجتمع أمتي على الضلال يقتضي عدم خروج الحق عن الأمة ولعله لذلك يكون قول الإمام محمد المهدي الموعود حجة يخطىء مخالفه وقيل (لا أي لا يكون حجة (لأن المنفي عنه الخطأ الاجتماع دون الواحد (وهو المختار) وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه إنما نفي عن الإجماع الخطأ تكريماً لهذه الأمة المرحومة لعدم خروج الحق عنها وهو يقتضي نفي الخطأ عن الواحد إذا كان هو المجتهد كيف لا ويلزم حينئذ أن لا يكون في الأمة من يأمر بالمعروف وينهي عن المنكر والسمعي ينفيه فافهم.
Issue: The number of tawatur is not required in the mujtami'in, according to the chosen view of the majority. The intended meaning is not a specific number, for it has preceded that there is no minimum limit. Rather, it means a number that, if they inform about a sensory matter, knowledge occurs. Because authority is only for the agreement, as an honor for this community, and it is absolute with no role for tawatur number. Know that the mainstay in proving the authority of this consensus is scriptural proofs. As for rational proofs, they do not benefit because pointing out error is not apparent for the opponent of the consensus who do not reach the number of tawatur, as is not hidden. Hence, the author said: the authority of consensus is devotional, as an honor, so understand. Some said: a group is necessary, and the agreement of two, even if they are the entire community of mujtahids, is not consensus because of the hadith reproaching opposing the group. Others said: two suffice if they are the entire community of mujtahids, and it is apparent; otherwise, it would necessitate the community agreeing on error. As for one person, if he is the only mujtahid, it is said it is proof, so that truth does not leave the community, and the verification of the criterion 'My community will not agree on error' necessitates that truth does not leave the community. Perhaps for this reason, the statement of Imam Muhammad al-Mahdi, the Promised, is proof; his opponent is wrong. Others said no, it is not proof, because error is negated from the collective, not the individual. And it is the chosen view. And you should not be unaware that error is negated from consensus as an honor for this merciful community, so that truth does not leave it. This necessitates negating error from the individual if he is the mujtahid. How not? Otherwise, there would be no one in the community to command good and forbid evil, and scriptural proofs negate that. So understand.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage addresses the number of scholars required for ijma to be hujja. The author clarifies that ijma does not require the number of tawatur (mass transmission). The authority of ijma is due to the agreement itself as an honor for the ummah, not due to a specific count. The text then discusses three opinions: (1) Some say a group (jamā‘a) is needed, and the agreement of two (even if they are the only mujtahids) is not ijma because of the hadith blaming opposing the group. (2) Others say two suffice if they are the entire ummah of mujtahids, and this is apparent, otherwise it would imply the ummah agreeing on error. (3) The third opinion considers a single mujtahid: if he is the only mujtahid, his opinion is hujja so that truth does not leave the ummah, supported by the hadith 'My community will not agree on error.' The chosen view is that a single mujtahid's opinion is hujja, because negating error from the community includes the individual when he is the only one, otherwise there would be no one to enjoin good. The passage emphasizes that the authority is devotional (ta‘abbudī) as an honor.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Mass transmission; a number that produces certainty in sensory matters; not required for ijma
عدد التواتر (‘adad al-tawātur): The specific number associated with tawatur; it is not fixed and not required for ijma
اجتماع (ijtimā‘): Agreement, the collective opinion; the basis for ijma
الحجية تعبدي (al-ḥujjiyya ta‘abbudī): The authority of something is devotional (based on divine command) rather than rational; used for ijma

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) His opinion is not considered ijma because error is negated from the collective only.
B) His opinion is considered ijma and is hujja because otherwise truth would leave the ummah.
C) Two persons are required, based on hadith.
D) Tawatur number is required.

Key Takeaway
Ijma does not require a specific number of scholars; the chosen Hanafi view holds that even a single mujtahid can represent the ummah's consensus, ensuring truth never departs from the community.

The Tabi'i Mujtahid and Sahaba Ijma: A Usul Dispute
Discusses whether a tabi'i mujtahid's opposition prevents Sahaba's ijma from being hujja.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers a tabi'i mujtahid's opposition to Sahaba's ijma as preventing that ijma from being hujja, and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
A tabi'i mujtahid's opposition breaks Sahaba's ijma because infallibility belongs to the entire ummah.

The concept of ijma (consensus) is a primary source of Islamic law. But whose consensus? This lesson examines a key usul dispute: when the Sahaba (Companions) have all agreed on a ruling, does the disagreement of a tabi'i (a scholar from the next generation) matter? The Hanafi position, shared by the majority of theologians, is that it does. Understanding this dispute sharpens our understanding of the scope of infallibility ('isma) and the conditions for valid ijma.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The Hanafi (and Shafi'i, Ash'ari) position is that a tabi'i mujtahid is considered. If he opposes the Sahaba, their agreement is not a binding ijma. Find the statement of this position in the text.
Look for 'عند الحنفية والشافعية وأكثر المتكلمين'.
2
Examine the objection and response
An objector argues that opposing the Sahaba is haram, so the tabi'i's opinion is irrelevant. The Hanafi response: if his ijtihad leads him to a different conclusion based on weak speculation, it is not haram. Locate this exchange in the passage.
The objection starts with 'فإن قلت' and the response with 'قلت'.
3
Understand the condition for later mujtahids
The text adds that a tabi'i who reaches ijtihad after the Sahaba's ijma is considered only if the 'asr (era) has not ended and no opposition appeared from the original consensus-makers. This refines the rule.
Condition: 'موقوف على شرط انقراض العصر وعدم ظهور المخالفة'.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
Some (a narration from Imam Ahmad) hold that the tabi'i is never considered. The Hanafi proof (dalil) is that infallibility ('isma) is for the entire ummah, so the tabi'i's opinion is part of that infallible body.
The Hanafi proof: 'لنا العصمة تثبت للكل من الأمة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: التابعي المجتهد معتبر عند انعقاد إجماع الصحابة عند الحنفية والشافعية وأكثر المتكلمين) فلا يكون إجماعاً عند مخالفته إياهم، فإن قلت هذا لا من يقول بحجية عند يصح قول الصحابة، فإن مخالفة التابعي إياه حرام عليه فلا يعتبر قوله فلا يضر إجماعهم، قلت لا نسلم الحرمة عنده إذا أدى اجتهاده إلى عدم الحجية لكونها مجتهداً فيها مظنونة ظناً ضعيفاً فافهم (ومن بلغ درجة الاجتهاد بعد إجماعهم فاعتباره موقوف على شرط انقراض العصر وعدم ظهور المخالفة من المجمعين بعد الإجماع ولا) من (التابعين إياهم في حياتهم) فعند هذا الشارط لا بد من دخول من بلغ الاجتهاد زمن الصحابة بعد إجماعهم (وقيل لا يعتد) التابعي في إجماعهم مطلقاً وهو رواية عن الإمام (أحمد) وإليه يشير كلمات الشيخ الأكبر (لنا العصمة) تثبت للكل) من الأمة والصحابة مع وجود هذا التابعي بعض الأمة (أقول : إن قيل لولا (قاطع عندهم على الحكم لما أجمعوا عادة عليه فيكون إجماعهم حجة ولا ينظر إلى
Issue: The tabi'i mujtahid is considered when the ijma of the Sahaba is formed, according to the Hanafis, Shafi'is, and most theologians. So it is not ijma when he opposes them. If you say: This is not from those who say that the statement of the Sahaba is hujja, because opposing them is haram for him, so his statement is not considered, and thus does not harm their ijma. I say: We do not accept the prohibition in his case, when his ijtihad leads to the conclusion of non-authority, because it is a matter of ijtihad based on a weak speculation, so understand. And whoever reaches the degree of ijtihad after their ijma, his being considered is conditional on the extinction of the era and the non-appearance of opposition from the mujtami'in after the ijma, and also from the tabi'in during their lives. According to this condition, it is necessary that he who reached ijtihad during the time of the Sahaba after their ijma is included. Others said: The tabi'i is not considered in their ijma at all, which is a narration from Imam Ahmad, and the words of the great shaykh allude to it. Our proof: Infallibility is established for the entire community, and the Sahaba along with the existence of this tabi'i are part of the community. I say: If it is said: Unless there was a definitive proof for them on the ruling, they would not normally have agreed upon it; so their ijma is hujja and no attention is paid to...
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage addresses whether a tabi'i mujtahid (a scholar from the generation after the Sahaba) is considered when the Sahaba have formed an ijma. The Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Ash'ari position is that if such a tabi'i opposes, the ijma is not valid because his opinion is considered. An objection is raised: opposing the Sahaba is haram, so his opinion is irrelevant. The response: if his ijtihad leads him to believe that the Sahaba's position is not authoritative (based on weak speculation), then it is not haram for him to oppose. The text then discusses the condition for considering a later mujtahid: he must have reached ijtihad during the time of the Sahaba and before the extinction of the era, and there must be no opposition from the original mujtami'in. Some narrations from Imam Ahmad say the tabi'i is never considered. The Hanafi proof is that infallibility is for the entire ummah, and the Sahaba together with the tabi'i constitute the ummah; so if the tabi'i opposes, the ummah is not unanimous, and thus no ijma.

Key Terms
تابعي (tābi‘ī): A Muslim from the generation after the Sahaba who met at least one Sahabi; a mujtahid among them is considered in ijma
مجتهد (mujtahid): One who has the qualifications to derive rulings from the evidence
عصمة (‘iṣma): Infallibility; the attribute of the Muslim community that prevents it from agreeing on error

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis and majority, what is the status of a tabi'i mujtahid when the Sahaba have reached an agreement?
A) His opposition is irrelevant because he must follow Sahaba.
B) His opposition prevents the agreement from being ijma.
C) He is not considered because he came after.
D) His opinion is respected but does not affect the ijma.

Key Takeaway
A tabi'i mujtahid's opposition prevents the Sahaba's consensus from being a binding ijma because infallibility attaches to the entire ummah, not just the Companions.

Definition of Ijma' and Its Scope
Defines ijma' and addresses objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ijma' according to Hanafi usul and explain its scope in relation to qati' texts.

Core Idea
Ijma' is binding only where no conclusive textual proof (qati') exists.

This lesson introduces the third source of Islamic law: Ijma' (consensus). The Hanafi school defines it precisely: it applies only to matters where there is no definitive textual evidence (qati'), leaving room for ijtihad. The passage also addresses two objections raised by critics, clarifying the conditions and validity of ijma'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and condition
Read the first part of the passage: 'الأصل الثالث الإجماع الإجماع أي على أن ما لا قاطع فيه محل الاجتهاد'. What is the condition for ijma' to be applicable?
The key term is 'ما لا قاطع فيه' – matters without a conclusive proof.
2
State the first objection and the Hanafi response
The objectors say that defining ijma' as such leads to contradictions (لزم النقيضان). How does the author respond? Find the 'حل' (solution).
The response: The absence of ruling due to absence of attribute does not nullify the agreed-upon matter.
3
State the second objection and the Hanafi response
The second objection is about considering ijma' of later generations despite early disagreements among Sahaba. The author rejects the implication. Identify the reasoning.
Key phrase: 'نمنع الملازمة' – we deny the implication. The difference is that when earlier disagreement is established, subsequent agreement cannot override it.
4
Recognize the epistemological weight
The passage ends by noting that ijma' is a proof (حجة) according to the majority, but only when prior disagreement is absent (ما لم يكن خلاف سابق). Understand this condition.
This reflects the Hanafi stance that ijma' after established disagreement is not valid; otherwise, the consequent is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثالث الإجماع الإجماع أي على أن ما لا قاطع فيه محل الاجتهاد فحينئذ لزم النقيضان (والحل أنه في العرف عرفية عامة أي ما لا قاطع فيه محل الاجتهاد ما دام لا (قاطع فيه فانعدام الحكم لانعدام الوصف لا يوجب بطلان هذا الذي هو مجمع عليه (و) قالوا (ثانياً: لو اعتبر) اجماع من بعدهم لاعتبر مع مخالفة بعض الصحابة بعضاً، يعني لو اعتبر هذا الاجماع لاعتبر اجماع من بعد الصحابة بعد تقرر الخلاف فيهم قلنا : نمنع الملازمة فإن بينهما فرقاً بعدم وجود الاتفاق عند استقرار الخلاف السابق فيمن قبل لكون قول كل مع الدليل حقاً، هذا عند من يشترط عدم الخلاف السابق أو بطلان اللازم فإن هذا الإجماع حجة أيضاً على رأي الأكثر .
The third principle: Ijma'. Ijma' means that what has no conclusive proof is subject to ijtihad. Then two contradictories would follow. The solution is that it is a common custom, i.e., what has no conclusive proof is subject to ijtihad as long as there is no conclusive proof. So the absence of the ruling due to the absence of the attribute does not nullify this which is agreed upon. They said, secondly: If the consensus of those after them were considered, it would be considered despite some Sahaba differing from others, meaning if this consensus were considered, then consensus after the Sahaba would be considered after the establishment of disagreement among them. We say: We deny the implication; there is a difference between them due to the absence of agreement when the previous disagreement is established among the former, because each opinion is true along with its proof. This is according to those who stipulate the absence of prior disagreement; otherwise the consequent is invalid, for this consensus is also a proof according to the majority opinion.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a definition of ijma' (consensus) as the third source of Islamic law. The author clarifies that ijma' applies only to matters where there is no conclusive textual proof (qati'), as such matters are subject to ijtihad. The passage then addresses two objections. First objection: If ijma' is defined as such, it could lead to contradictions. The response: The ruling is conditioned on the absence of a qati' proof, so the absence of such proof does not invalidate the consensus. Second objection: If consensus of later generations is accepted despite disagreement among Sahaba, it would create inconsistency. The response: The cases are different because when earlier disagreement is established, no subsequent agreement can be formed that overrides it. The majority holds that such consensus is a proof.

Key Terms
قاطع (qati'): Conclusive textual proof from Quran or sunnah
محل الاجتهاد (mahall al-ijtihad): Matters open to ijtihad because no definitive text exists
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of mujtahids on a legal ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, ijma' applies only to matters that have what characteristic?
A) Matters with a clear Quranic text
B) Matters where there is no conclusive proof (qati')
C) Matters that are universally accepted by all Muslims
D) Matters of ritual worship only

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a binding proof only in the absence of a definitive textual proof (qati').

Al-Ijma — Consensus

8 min
Status of a Tabi'i Mujtahid in the Ijma' of the Sahaba
Ruling on whether a tabi'i's opposition prevents sahaba's ijma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on the consideration of a tabi'i mujtahid in Sahaba's ijma' and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
A tabi'i mujtahid's opposition prevents ijma', but his view remains a speculative proof.

This lesson explores a key usul al-fiqh question: when the Sahaba reach a consensus on a ruling, does the opposition of a tabi'i who has reached ijtihad invalidate that consensus? The Hanafi school, along with the Shafi'is and most mutakallimun, holds that the tabi'i is considered, and his disagreement prevents the formation of binding ijma'. However, his opinion is not conclusive but is treated as a speculative proof. This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' lays out the argument, including the evidence from the practice of the Sahaba and the famous incident regarding the waiting period of a pregnant widow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The tabi'i mujtahid is considered; his opposition prevents the Sahaba's consensus from being a binding ijma'.
This is the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and majority mutakallimun position.
2
Analyze the objection
The objection states that a tabi'i must follow the Sahaba because their consensus is based on certainty, so his opposition is sinful and irrelevant.
The objection relies on the assumption that the Sahaba's consensus is always based on a conclusive proof.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response denies that the consensus is necessarily based on certainty; it may be based on qiyas. The Sahaba themselves permitted ijtihad alongside them, as shown in the incident of Subai'ah al-Aslamiyyah.
The permission indicates that the Sahaba considered the tabi'i's opinion.
4
Apply the condition of inqirad al-'asr
If a tabi'i reaches ijtihad after the Sahaba's consensus but while the era is still ongoing, his consideration is conditional on the non-appearance of opposition from the consensus members and the passage of the era.
This determines whether a later mujtahid's view can affect an earlier ijma'.
5
Determine the epistemological status
The tabi'i's opinion is a speculative proof (hujja zanniyya), not certain. It must be weighed against the Sahaba's consensus, which is also speculative in nature.
The passage concludes that the truth is that it is a speculative proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: التابعي المجتهد معتبر عند انعقاد إجماع الصحابة عند الحنفية والشافعية وأكثر المتكلمين) فلا يكون إجماعاً عند مخالفته إياهم، فإن قلت هذا لا من يقول بحجية عند يصح قول الصحابة، فإن مخالفة التابعي إياه حرام عليه فلا يعتبر قوله فلا يضر إجماعهم، قلت لا نسلم الحرمة عنده إذا أدى اجتهاده إلى عدم الحجية لكونها مجتهداً فيها مظنونة ظناً ضعيفاً فافهم (ومن بلغ درجة الاجتهاد بعد إجماعهم فاعتباره موقوف على شرط انقراض العصر وعدم ظهور المخالفة من المجمعين بعد الإجماع ولا) من (التابعين إياهم في حياتهم) فعند هذا الشارط لا بد من دخول من بلغ الاجتهاد زمن الصحابة بعد إجماعهم (وقيل لا يعتد) التابعي في إجماعهم مطلقاً وهو رواية عن الإمام (أحمد) وإليه يشير كلمات الشيخ الأكبر (لنا العصمة) تثبت للكل) من الأمة والصحابة مع وجود هذا التابعي بعض الأمة (أقول : إن قيل لولا (قاطع عندهم على الحكم لما أجمعوا عادة عليه فيكون إجماعهم حجة ولا ينظر إلى معهم قول التابعي (قلنا ممنوع) فإن الاتفاق قد يكون بالقياس واستدل بأنهم سوغوا الاجتهاد معهم كسعيد وشريح والحسن ونحوهم ولولا الاعتبار) لهم (لم يفد) تسويغهم اجتهاداً أجيب إنما يتم لو ثبت التسويغ مع إجماعهم يعني إنما يتم لو ثبت تسويغهم إياه في إجماعهم وهو ممنوع (لا) فيما يكون مختلفا فيه فإنّ التسويغ فيه لا يفيد ما نحن فيه (كما عن أبي سلمة تذاكرت مع ابن عباس وأبي هريرة في عدة الحامل لوفاة زوجها فقال ابن عباس بأبعد الأجلين وقلت بوضع الحمل ولفظ البخاري : جاء رجل إلى ابن عباس وأبو هريرة جالس عنده فقال : أفتني في امرأة ولدت بعد زوجها بأربعين ليلة ؟ فقال ابن عباس : بأبعد الأجلين فقلت أنا ﴿ وَأُوَلَتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَن يَضَعْنَ حَمَلَهُنَّ ﴾ [الطلاق: ٤] فقال أبو هريرة: أنا مع ابن أخي، يعني أبا سلمة فأرسل ابن عباس كريباً إلى أم سلمة فقالت : قتل زوج سبيعة الأسلمية وهي حبلى، فوضعت بعد موته بأربعين ليلة فحطبت فأنكحها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وكان أبو السنابل فيمن خطبها . واعلم أنهم اختلفوا بعد أن الإجماع مع مخالفة التابعي المجتهد ليس إجماعاً إنه حجة أم لا فمن ذهب إلى حجية قول الصحابي يقول حجة ومن لا فينبغي لا والحق أنه حجة مظنونة لظهور إصابة رأي هؤلاء الأخيار المشاهدين للقرائن فافهم.
Issue: The mujtahid tabi'i is considered in the formation of ijma' of the Sahaba according to the Hanafis, Shafi'is, and most mutakallimun. So it is not ijma' when he opposes them. If you say: This is not according to those who say the statement of a Sahabi is a proof, for the tabi'i's opposition to him is prohibited for him, so his statement is not considered and does not harm their ijma'. I say: We do not concede the prohibition in his view, if his ijtihad leads to the absence of authority, because it is a matter of ijtihad with a weak speculative proof, so understand. And one who reaches the level of ijtihad after their ijma', his consideration is dependent on the condition of the extinction of the era and the non-appearance of opposition from those forming consensus after the ijma', and also from the tabi'in during their lifetime. According to this condition, it is necessary to include one who reached ijtihad in the time of the Sahaba after their ijma'. And it was said: The tabi'i is not considered in their ijma' at all, and this is a narration from Imam Ahmad, and the words of the greatest shaykh indicate it. Our proof: Infallibility ('ismah) is established for the whole ummah, and the Sahaba along with this tabi'i are part of the ummah. I say: If it is said: Were there not a conclusive proof for them regarding the ruling, they would not have normally formed ijma' upon it; thus their ijma' is a proof and the tabi'i's statement is not considered. We say: This is denied, because agreement may be through qiyas. And they argued that they permitted ijtihad alongside them, like Sa'id, Shuraih, al-Hasan, and others; and were it not for consideration (of their views), their permission for ijtihad would not be beneficial. The response: This would only be if the permission was established along with their ijma', i.e., it must be proven that they permitted him in their ijma', which is denied. Not in matters of difference; for permission therein does not benefit our case. As reported from Abu Salama: I discussed with Ibn Abbas and Abu Huraira regarding the waiting period of a pregnant widow. Ibn Abbas said: The longer of the two terms, and I said: By giving birth. The wording of Bukhari: A man came to Ibn Abbas while Abu Huraira was sitting with him and said: Give me a fatwa regarding a woman who gave birth forty nights after her husband's death? Ibn Abbas said: The longer of the two terms. I said: I (recite) 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth' (65:4). Abu Huraira said: I am with my nephew, meaning Abu Salama. So Ibn Abbas sent Kuraib to Umm Salama, and she said: The husband of Subai'ah al-Aslamiyyah was killed while she was pregnant, and she gave birth forty nights after his death, so she was proposed to, and the Messenger of Allah married her, and Abu al-Sanabil was among those who proposed. Know that they differed after that: The ijma' with the opposition of a mujtahid tabi'i is not ijma', but is it a proof or not? Those who hold the statement of a Sahabi as a proof say it is a proof; those who do not, say it is not. The truth is that it is a speculative proof, because of the apparent correctness of the opinion of these good people who witnessed the indications, so understand.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the status of a tabi'i (successor) mujtahid when the Sahaba have formed ijma'. The Hanafi, Shafi'i, and majority position is that the tabi'i is considered; his opposition prevents the Sahaba's agreement from being binding ijma'. The passage responds to an objection that a tabi'i must follow the Sahaba, arguing that if his ijtihad leads him to a different conclusion, he is not sinful to differ. It then discusses the time condition: if a person reaches ijtihad after the Sahaba's ijma' but while some are still alive, his consideration is conditional on the 'extinction of the era' and no opposition from the ijma' participants. An alternative view (from Imam Ahmad) says the tabi'i is never considered. The proof for the Hanafi view is that the Sahaba themselves allowed ijtihad alongside them, as seen in the example of Ibn Abbas and Abu Huraira regarding the pregnant widow's iddah. The passage concludes that the opinion of a tabi'i who opposes the Sahaba's consensus is a speculative proof (hujja zanniyya), not a certain one.

Key Terms
التابعي المجتهد (al-tabi'i al-mujtahid): A successor who has reached the level of ijtihad
انقراض العصر (inqirad al-'asr): The passing of all the mujtahids of a generation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid and sinful
B) It prevents the consensus from being ijma', but is itself a speculative proof
C) It is completely ignored
D) It overrides the Sahaba's consensus

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers a tabi'i mujtahid's opposition sufficient to prevent binding ijma', but his opinion remains a speculative proof.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

Majority Consensus as Ijma': Hanafi Position
Ruling on majority consensus as ijma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on whether majority consensus is ijma' and evaluate its evidentiary weight using the condition of 'kull'.

Core Idea
Majority consensus is not ijma' because infallibility requires agreement of all, but it may still be a strong speculative proof.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, ijma' is a definitive proof only when it is unanimous. But what if a large majority agrees and only one or two scholars dissent? This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut examines that question, presenting historical examples and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position. You will learn why the majority opinion without unanimity does not qualify as ijma' and how it is treated as a speculative proof (hujja zanniyya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage asks whether the consensus of the majority (ijma' al-akthar) with only one or two dissenters counts as ijma'. Recognize that this is a dispute about the definition of ijma' and its evidentiary strength.
2
Examine the examples given
The text lists cases: consensus on al-'awl (excluding Ibn Abbas), on nullification of wudu by sleep (excluding Abu Musa), and on fasting while traveling (excluding Abu Huraira and Ibn Umar). Note how each involves a single or very few dissenters from the majority.
The example of Abu Bakr and the zakat refusers is explained as not being a case of majority with dissent, because eventually all Sahaba agreed.
3
Understand the chosen view (mukhtar)
The passage states 'al-mukhtar annahu laysa bi-ijma'' — the chosen view is that it is not ijma'. The reason is that infallibility ('isma) is attached to the whole ummah (kull), not the majority. So majority alone does not guarantee infallibility.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: unanimity is required for ijma'.
4
Analyze the two positions on evidentiary value
Even though it is not ijma', there is a difference of opinion on whether majority consensus is a proof (hujja) at all. Some say it is not a proof; others say it is a speculative proof (hujja zanniyya) because the majority is unlikely to err after thorough investigation.
The text provides a counter-argument: truth may be with the minority, citing the hadith of the saved sect being one of seventy-three.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: if majority consensus were ijma', it would be infallible and binding on all. Since it is not, it may be followed as a strong opinion but does not carry the same binding force. A mufti can prefer it but is not compelled to.
This affects how a ruling based on majority opinion is treated in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : قيل إجماع الأكثر مع ندرة المخالف بأن يكون واحداً أو اثنين (إجماع كغير ابن عباس أجمعوا على القول بالعول) عند تكثر السهام عن المال هذا على المشهور، وإلا فسيجيء أن إنكار العول مما لم يصح عنه وغير أبي موسى الأشعري أجمعوا على نقض النوم للوضوء، وغير أبي هريرة وابن عمر أجمعوا على جواز الصوم في السفر) فيه إشارة إلى أن أبا هريرة فقيه كما هو الصحيح وقد مر (وقيل إن سوغ الأكثر اجتهاده) مع مخالفته إياهم (كخلاف) أمير المؤمنين وإمام الصديقين أبي بكر الصديق في الممتنعين عن أداء (الصدقات) حيث تفرد بالحكم بقتلهم فلا ينعقد الإجماع مع مخالفته بخلاف قول ابن عباس بحل التفاضل في أموال الربا فإنهم لم يسوغوا اجتهاده هذا حتى أنكروا عليه مرة بعد أخرى إلى أن عما كان يقول كما في صحيح مسلم وروي عنه اللهم إني تبت عن قولي في الصرف وقولي في المتعة، وفي التمثيل الأول نظر فإنه لم يثبت أن غير أمير المؤمنين الصديق الأكبر اتفقوا على عدم جواز قتال مانعي الزكاة وهو رضي الله تعالى عنه خالفهم فقط، بل الذي ثبت رضي الله عنه لما هم بقتال مانعي الزكاة اشتبه ذلك على أمير المؤمنين عمر بقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله فكشف شبهته بأنه داخل في الاستثناء فوافقه وأجمع عليه الصحابة كافة وقاتلوا معه فليس هذا من الباب في شيء فاحفظه (والمختار أنه ليس بإجماع لانتفاء (الكل) الذي هو مناط العصمة، ثم اختلفوا (فقيل ليس بحجة أصلاً) كما أنه ليس بإجماع (وقيل: بل حجة ظنية) غير الإجماع (لأن الظاهر إصابة السواد الأعظم) إذ من البعيد أن لا يطلع الأكثر بعد الفحص الشديد ويطلع الواحد الأندر (قيل ربما كان الحق الأقل) وليس فيه بعد ألا ترى الفرقة الناجية واحدة من ثلاث وسبعين).
Issue: It was said that the consensus of the majority with rare dissent, i.e., one or two, is ijma', like (the consensus) of other than Ibn Abbas on the doctrine of al-'awl (increase of shares) when the shares exceed the estate, according to the well-known view; otherwise it will come that the denial of 'awl is not authentically reported from him. And other than Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, they agreed on the nullification of wudu by sleep. And other than Abu Huraira and Ibn Umar, they agreed on the permissibility of fasting while traveling. In this there is an indication that Abu Huraira was a jurist, as is correct, and it has passed. And it was said: If the majority permitted his ijtihad despite his opposition to them, like the opposition of the Commander of the Faithful, Imam Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, regarding those who refused to pay the zakat, where he uniquely ruled to fight them, then ijma' is not formed with his opposition. Unlike the statement of Ibn Abbas on the permissibility of riba al-fadl, for they did not permit his ijtihad in this, rather they rebuked him repeatedly until he retracted what he said, as in Sahih Muslim, and it is reported that he said: O Allah, I repent from my statement on currency exchange and from my statement on mut'ah. In the first example there is consideration, because it is not established that other than the Commander of the Faithful, the Greater truthful one, agreed on the impermissibility of fighting the zakat refusers, and he only alone opposed them. Rather, what is established is that when he intended to fight them, it was ambiguous to Umar due to the Prophet's saying: I have been commanded to fight people until they say there is no god but Allah. He clarified the ambiguity by saying that they fall under the exception, so he agreed, and all the Sahaba formed consensus on it and fought with him. So this is not of this category at all, so preserve it. The chosen view is that it is not ijma', because the whole (kull) which is the basis of infallibility is absent. Then they differed: Some said it is not a proof at all, just as it is not ijma'. Others said: Rather it is a speculative proof, other than ijma', because the apparent is that the great majority is correct, as it is unlikely that the majority, after thorough investigation, would not arrive at the truth while the rare one does. It was said: Perhaps the truth is with the minority, and there is no impossibility in this. Do you not see that the saved sect is one out of seventy-three?
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on whether the consensus of the majority with only one or two dissenters counts as ijma'. The text presents both sides. Examples are given: consensus on 'awl (increase of shares) excluding Ibn Abbas, on nullification of wudu by sleep excluding Abu Musa, on fasting in travel excluding Abu Huraira and Ibn Umar. The key distinction is whether the majority permitted the dissenter's ijtihad. The case of Abu Bakr fighting zakat refusers is analyzed: initially there was doubt, but then all Sahaba agreed, so it was not a case of majority with dissent. The chosen view (mukhtar) is that such majority agreement is not ijma' because the condition of 'all' (kull) is absent. However, there is disagreement on its authority: some say it is not a proof at all, others say it is a speculative proof (hujja zanniyya) because the majority is likely correct. The text acknowledges that truth can be with the minority, citing the hadith that the saved sect is one of seventy-three.

Key Terms
السواد الأعظم (al-sawad al-a'zam): The great majority; the larger group of scholars
حجة ظنية (hujja zanniyya): A speculative proof; binding in practice but not certain
الكل (al-kull): The whole; all qualified mujtahids

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (mukhtar) in this passage, what is the ruling on the consensus of the majority with one or two dissenters?
A) It is a binding ijma'
B) It is not ijma' but a speculative proof
C) It is rejected completely
D) It is considered ijma' only in ritual matters

Key Takeaway
Majority consensus is not ijma' in Hanafi usul because infallibility attaches to the whole ummah (kull), not the majority; however, it may serve as a strong speculative proof.

Opposing a Tabi'i to Ijma' and its Hujjiyya
Usul dispute on the evidentiary value of ijma' with Tabi'i opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether ijma' with a Tabi'i's opposition constitutes a binding proof and identify its epistemological status in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A Tabi'i's opposition does not break the hujjiyya of ijma'; it remains a zanni proof.

When a Tabi'i (follower) opposes the consensus of the Companions, does that consensus retain any evidentiary authority? This lesson examines the Hanafi view that such ijma' is a zanni (conjectural) proof, not qat'i, and explores the reasoning behind it through a classical story and scholarly analysis.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core question: does the opposition of a single Tabi'i (mujtahid) break the hujjiyya of the ijma' of the Companions?
2
Analyze the argument against Tabi'i ijtihad
The text begins by rejecting the idea that Tabi'i ijtihad is permitted if it contradicts consensus, because permission would need to be proven from the Companions themselves.
Focus on the phrase 'قول التابعي (قلنا ممنوع)'
3
Examine the historical evidence
Study the story of Abu Salama, Ibn Abbas, and Abu Huraira on the idda of a pregnant widow. Note how the Tabi'i's view was supported by a Companion (Umm Salama) and the Prophet's practice.
This shows that a Tabi'i can be correct, but does not negate the weight of the majority view.
4
Evaluate the different positions on hujjiyya
Contrast the view that the majority view has no authority (opposing school) with the view that it is a binding proof (based on qawl al-sahabi). Identify the Hanafi middle ground.
The text states 'الحق أنه حجة مظنونة' (the truth is it is a conjectural proof).
5
Derive the Hanafi position
Conclude that the ijma' with a Tabi'i's opposition is a zanni hujja due to the high probability that the Companions are correct, but it does not reach certainty.
This affects how judges and muftis weigh evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معهم
قول التابعي (قلنا ممنوع) فإن الاتفاق قد يكون بالقياس واستدل بأنهم سوغوا الاجتهاد معهم كسعيد وشريح والحسن ونحوهم ولولا الاعتبار) لهم (لم يفد) تسويغهم اجتهاداً أجيب إنما يتم لو ثبت التسويغ مع إجماعهم يعني إنما يتم لو ثبت تسويغهم إياه في إجماعهم وهو ممنوع (لا) فيما يكون مختلفا فيه فإنّ التسويغ فيه لا يفيد ما نحن فيه (كما عن أبي سلمة تذاكرت مع ابن عباس وأبي هريرة في عدة الحامل لوفاة زوجها فقال ابن عباس بأبعد الأجلين وقلت بوضع الحمل ولفظ البخاري : جاء رجل إلى ابن عباس وأبو هريرة جالس عنده فقال : أفتني في امرأة ولدت بعد زوجها بأربعين ليلة ؟ فقال ابن عباس : بأبعد الأجلين فقلت أنا ﴿ وَأُوَلَتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَن يَضَعْنَ حَمَلَهُنَّ ﴾ [الطلاق: ٤] فقال أبو هريرة: أنا مع ابن أخي، يعني أبا سلمة فأرسل ابن عباس كريباً إلى أم سلمة فقالت : قتل زوج سبيعة الأسلمية وهي حبلى، فوضعت بعد موته بأربعين ليلة فحطبت فأنكحها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وكان أبو السنابل فيمن خطبها .
واعلم أنهم اختلفوا بعد أن الإجماع مع مخالفة التابعي المجتهد ليس إجماعاً إنه حجة أم لا فمن ذهب إلى حجية قول الصحابي يقول حجة ومن لا فينبغي لا والحق أنه حجة مظنونة لظهور إصابة رأي هؤلاء الأخيار المشاهدين للقرائن فافهم.
With them. The statement of the Tabi'i (we said: forbidden) because agreement may be by analogy. And they argued that they permitted ijtihad with them like Sa'id, Shurayh, al-Hasan, and others. Were it not for consideration for them, their permitting ijtihad would not benefit. It was answered: This is only valid if permission was established with their consensus, meaning it is only valid if their permission is established in their consensus, and it is forbidden. Not in what is disputed, because permission in it does not benefit what we are discussing. As reported from Abu Salama: I discussed with Ibn Abbas and Abu Huraira about the waiting period of a pregnant woman whose husband died. Ibn Abbas said: the longer of the two terms, and I said: by delivering the pregnancy. The wording of Bukhari: A man came to Ibn Abbas while Abu Huraira was sitting with him. He said: Give me a ruling on a woman who gave birth forty nights after her husband? Ibn Abbas said: the longer of the two terms. I said: {And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their pregnancy} [At-Talaq: 4]. Abu Huraira said: I am with my brother's son, meaning Abu Salama. So Ibn Abbas sent Kurayb to Umm Salama, and she said: The husband of Subay'a al-Aslamiyya was killed while she was pregnant, and she gave birth forty nights after his death, so she was sought in marriage, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married her. Abu al-Sanabil was among those who proposed. And know that they differed: after it is established that ijma' with the opposition of a mujtahid Tabi'i is not ijma', is it a proof or not? Whoever holds the proof of the Companion's statement says it is a proof, and whoever does not, should say no. The truth is that it is a conjectural proof because of the apparent correctness of the opinion of these good people who witnessed the circumstances. So understand.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on whether a Tabi'i (follower) who opposes the consensus of the Companions affects the hujjiyya (evidentiary authority) of that consensus. The author begins by addressing the claim that a Tabi'i's statement can be considered, but he refutes it: if the Tabi'i's ijtihad were permitted, it would only be valid if it were established that the Companions allowed such ijtihad in matters of their consensus, which is not proven. He then provides a historical example: Abu Salama, a Tabi'i, differed with Ibn Abbas and Abu Huraira on the 'idda of a pregnant widow. Ibn Abbas held she must wait the longer of the two terms, while Abu Salama argued she could remarry immediately after delivery, citing the Quranic verse. Abu Huraira sided with Abu Salama. They referred to Umm Salama, who confirmed that Subay'a al-Aslamiyya gave birth forty days after her husband's death and was married by the Prophet. This shows that even though the Companions Ibn Abbas and Abu Huraira initially differed, the Tabi'i's opinion was eventually supported by a Companion's report. The author then notes that scholars differ on whether such a consensus (with a Tabi'i opposing) is a hujja. Some rely on the principle that the Companion's statement is hujja, so they deem it a hujja. Others do not. The author opts for the middle ground: it is a zanni (conjectural) hujja, not qat'i, because the Tabi'i's view might also be correct.

Key Terms
التابعي (al-tābi‘ī): A Muslim who met the Companions but not the Prophet, and is considered a mujtahid in this context
الإجماع (al-ijmā‘): Consensus of all mujtahids of an age, here specifically of the Companions
حجة مظنونة (ḥujja maẓnūna): A proof that provides strong probability but not certainty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the story of Subay'a al-Aslamiyya, what was the initial difference of opinion between Ibn Abbas and Abu Salama?
A) Ibn Abbas said she must wait four months and ten days; Abu Salama said she could remarry immediately after delivery
B) Ibn Abbas said she must wait the longer of the two terms; Abu Salama said her term ends with delivery
C) Ibn Abbas said she must wait until she delivers; Abu Salama said she must wait four months and ten days
D) Ibn Abbas said she could remarry immediately; Abu Salama said she must wait the longer term

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school regards ijma' with a Tabi'i's opposition as a zanni (conjectural) proof, not a qat'i one.
